Rational Proof for Allah's Speech
Maturidi gives a rational argument from the absence of impediments.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational argument that Allah must be a speaker because silence implies an impediment incompatible with divine perfection.

Core Idea
A knower and powerful being who does not speak must have an impediment, and Allah is free from all impediments.

After citing revelation, Maturidi provides a rational proof based on analogy from the witnessed world. He argues that any being who knows and is powerful yet does not speak, does so because of some affliction such as incapacity or a defect. Since Allah is absolutely perfect and beyond all defects, He must be a speaker. Furthermore, speech is the most praiseworthy attribute, so it is fitting for Allah.

Guided Path
1
Read the rational proof passage
Read from 'وأما العقل' to the end of the source. Focus on the logical structure of the argument.
2
Understand the analogy from shahid
Maturidi observes that in the witnessed world, a person who knows and is able but does not speak has an impediment like deafness or dumbness. This is the starting point.
The shahid (witnessed world) provides a pattern that applies to the unseen by analogy (qiyas al-gha'ib 'ala al-shahid).
3
Negate impediments for Allah
Allah is free from all afflictions such as deafness, blindness, and dumbness. Therefore, He cannot lack speech due to an impediment.
4
Conclude that Allah is a speaker
Since there is no impediment, and being a knowing, powerful being, He must speak. Speech is also the most praiseworthy attribute.
The conclusion is that Allah is Mutakallim (Speaker) as a necessary attribute.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال أبو منصور رحمه الله : الأصل أن الله عز وجل قد ثبت وصفه بالكلام بحجة السمع والعقل ، فالسمع قوله وَكَلَّمَ اللهُ مُوسَى تَكْلِيمًا ذكره بالمصدر مع غير تمانع بين الخلق بكلام الله ، وقد وجد الاتفاق على أنه متكلم وأن له كلاما في الحقيقة وإن اختلفت الآراء في مائيته : ولا أنكر على الذين قالوا : لَوْلا يُكَلِّمُنَا الله إلا بوصف التكبر والجهل بمنزلة أنفسهم ، وكذلك قوله : وَقَدْ كَانَ فريقٌ مِنْهُم يَسْمَعُونَ كَلَامَ اللهِ
وأما العقل : إن كل عالم قادر لا يتكلم فعن آفة ، يكون من عجز أو والله عنه متعال ، ثبت أنه متكلم . على أن الذي لا يتكلم في الشاهد إنما لا يتكلم بالمعنى الذي لا يسمع ولا يبصر من الآفة ، والله منزه عن المعنى الذي يقتضى الصمم والعمى ، وكذلك البكم ، وهو أولى ; إذ هو أجل ما يحمد به
Abu Mansur (may Allah have mercy on him) said: The foundation is that Allah, mighty and majestic, has established His description with speech by the proof of revelation and reason. As for revelation, His saying: 'And Allah spoke to Moses directly' (4:164) mentioned in the verbal noun without any dissent among the creation regarding Allah's speech. And the agreement has been found that He is a speaker and that He has real speech, even if opinions differ on its quiddity. And I do not deny those who said: 'Why does not Allah speak to us?' (2:118) except by description of arrogance and ignorance of their own rank. Similarly, His saying: 'And a group among them used to listen to the words of Allah' (2:75).
As for reason: Every knower and powerful being who does not speak does so due to an impediment, whether from incapacity or [؟] – and Allah is exalted above that – so it is established that He is a speaker. Moreover, the one who does not speak in the witnessed world only does not speak in the sense that he does not hear or see due to an affliction. Allah is free from the meaning that necessitates deafness and blindness, and likewise dumbness. And it is more fitting, for it is the most praiseworthy thing by which He is praised.
Source pages p. 656

Commentary
This passage provides the proof for the attribute of speech (kalam). Maturidi states the foundational principle: Allah's description with speech is established by two types of evidence: sam' (revelation) and aql (reason). The scriptural proof includes the verse 'And Allah spoke to Moses directly' (4:164), which uses the emphatic verbal noun (takliman) to affirm real speech without any denial among the creation. There is agreement that Allah is Mutakallim (Speaker) and has real speech, though people differ on its nature (mahiyya). Maturidi criticizes those who demand 'Why does not Allah speak to us?' (2:118) as arrogant and ignorant of their own status. He also cites the verse 'a group among them used to listen to the words of Allah' (2:75) to show that Allah's speech is heard. The rational proof: every being who knows and has power yet does not speak, does so because of an impediment, either from incapacity or from [؟] – Allah is exalted above such defects – therefore it is established that He is a speaker. In the witnessed world (shahid), one who does not speak fails due to an affliction such as deafness or blindness. Allah is free from any meaning that necessitates deafness or blindness, and likewise dumbness. Speech is more fitting for Allah, as it is the most praiseworthy attribute by which He is praised.

Key Terms
العقل
كلام
آفة
الشاهد
متكلم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Allah does not speak because speech is a bodily function.
Correction: Maturidi shows that lack of speech in perfect beings is only due to impediments; Allah has no body or defects, so He must speak without letters or sounds.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi's rational argument, why must Allah be a speaker?
A) Because all powerful beings speak
B) Because silence implies an impediment, which cannot apply to Allah
C) Because the Quran explicitly states it
D) Because prophets reported it

Key Takeaway
Rational reasoning shows that Allah must be a speaker because silence would require an imperfection incompatible with His perfection.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You now know that Allah's silence would require an imperfection. Reflect on your own silence: when you neglect to speak about Allah's greatness, what impediment holds you back? Is it fear, laziness, or distraction? Will you commit to speaking one truth about Him today, even if only in your heart?
?
If Allah's speech is a perfection, what does your own speech reveal about your soul? Do you use words to praise Him, or are your conversations filled with silence about the One who constantly addresses you in the Quran? Starting tonight, will you let His speech transform what you say?
?
The proof shows that Allah speaks because He has no impediment. Can you say the same? Is there any impediment—pride, doubt, sin—that prevents you from hearing His speech as a living address to you? What will you remove today so you can respond?

Divine Attributes

God's Speech as an Essential Attribute
Maturidi argues that God's speech is not a separate entity but an essential attribute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's argument that God's speech is not a separate entity but an essential attribute of His essence.

Core Idea
God's speech is not other than Him; it is His essential attribute.

Imam Maturidi tackles a fundamental question about the nature of God's speech: is it something separate from God, or is it part of His very essence? Using a simple logical dilemma, he shows that if speech were separate, it would imply dependency and contingency—qualities incompatible with God. This short but powerful passage establishes the correct understanding of divine speech as an essential attribute.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic once, then the translation. Notice the crisp logical structure: 'either...or...'.
The Arabic is dense but clear.
2
Identify the two possibilities
Maturidi presents two options: speech is either 'other than Him' or 'not other than Him'. Mark these in the text.
3
Understand the consequences of each
If speech were other, it would remove a defect from God, implying need (hāja) and contingency (ḥadath)—unthinkable for God. If not other, then God is speaking by Himself.
The terms 'ghayr', 'hāja', and 'ḥadath' are key.
4
Draw the conclusion
Since the first option is absurd, the second must be true: God's speech is not separate but an essential attribute. Appreciate how Maturidi uses a simple dilemma to settle a deep theological point.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم لا يخلو من أن يكون غيره فيزول عنه ما ذكرنا من الآفة بغيره ، وذلك علم الحاجة وأمارة الحدث، أو ليس غيره فيكون بنفسه متكلما قادرا عالما.
وبالله التوفيق .
Then it cannot be free from either being other than Him, in which case the defect we mentioned would be removed from Him by that other — and that is a sign of need and a mark of contingency; or it is not other than Him, in which case He is by Himself speaking, powerful, knowing. And by Allah is success.
Source pages p. 657

Commentary
This passage presents a dilemma regarding the attribute of speech. Maturidi states that it cannot be free from one of two possibilities: either it is other (ghayr) than God, or it is not other. If it is other than God, then the defect (the need for speech) would be removed by that other, which would imply that God needs something else, indicating need (hāja) and contingency (ḥadath). If it is not other than God, meaning the attribute is identical with His essence, then God is by Himself speaking, powerful, and knowing — which is the correct view. Thus the speech of God is an essential attribute, not a separate entity. The passage ends with a prayer: 'And by Allah is success.'

Key Terms
غيره
الحاجة
الحدث
بنفسه

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That God's speech might be a created entity separate from His essence.
Correction: Maturidi shows that this would imply need and contingency in God, which is impossible. Therefore, God's speech is not other than Him.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, if God's speech were other than Him, what would that imply?
A) It would mean God is limited.
B) It would imply need and contingency.
C) It would make speech a creation.
D) It would contradict the Qur'an.

Key Takeaway
God's speech is not a separate entity but an essential attribute; otherwise it would imply need and contingency in God.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite the Quran, do you treat it as a mere book created in time, or as the very speech of Allah that is inseparable from His essence? How does this affect your reverence and attentiveness?
?
If God's speech were separate from Him, He would depend on it. How does knowing that His speech is His essential attribute change your understanding of His self-sufficiency and your personal need for His word?
?
The passage says God is speaking, powerful, and knowing by Himself. Do you truly seek His speech directly, or do you rely on intermediaries? What would change if you approached the Quran as a direct encounter with His attribute?

Divine Attributes

God's Speech is Unlike Created Speech
Maturidi argues that God's speech is incomparably different from human speech.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Maturidi argues that God's speech is fundamentally different from all created speech and how this difference negates temporality.

Core Idea
God's speech is entirely other — no measure or understanding can compare it to created speech.

Imam Maturidi presents a rigorous argument to establish the absolute transcendence of God's speech. He begins with the nature of human speech in the witnessed world, showing how it involves imitation and similarity. Then, using Quranic verses, he demonstrates that God is beyond all similarity, and that creation cannot produce anything like His speech. This leads to the conclusion that divine speech is not temporal and cannot be characterized by the attributes of created speech.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation once, noting the overall flow of the argument.
2
Identify the argument about human speech
Notice how Maturidi points out that human speech often involves imitation, implying similarity between speakers.
This sets up the need for divine transcendence.
3
Understand the Quranic proofs
Examine the two verses: 'There is nothing like unto Him' and 'They created like His creation' — how do they negate similarity?
The second verse shows that similarity in action would imply similarity in essence.
4
Consider the examples of non-human speech
What do the ant, hoopoe, and mountains teach us about the diversity of speech beyond human letters?
This demonstrates that some speech is beyond human comprehension.
5
Grasp the conclusion
How does the total opposition of God's speech to created speech negate temporality and other attributes?
If God's speech were like created speech, it would be subject to change and composition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
في الشاهد وبه ينفصل البشر من سائر الحيوان، مع ما كان كل محتمل الكلام. فعن عجز لا يتكلم أو عن سكوت. ثم لا يخلو من أن يكون على تقدير كلام غيره فيكون فيه تشابه، ودل قوله: لَيْسَ كَمِثْلِهِ شَيْءٌ على نفي الشبه له في الصفة والذات، وأيد ذلك قوله: خَلَقُوا كَخَلْقِهِ دل أن شبه الفعل يوجب التشابه، مع القول أن الخلق لو اجتمع لا يأتون بمثله فانتفى الشبه. إذ فيه تماثل، فثبت له المخالفة لكلام الخلق جميعا على ثبت لذاته، مع ما لم يمتحن جميع كلام الخلق ليدرك منتهى معانيه، وقد ذكر كلام النمل والهدهد وتسبيح الجبال وغيرها مما لا يفهم شيء من ذلك بالحروف المعجبة ولا على المفهوم من كلام البشر. وإذ ثبت أن من الكلام ما لا يبلغ تقديره وسع الخلق ولا يبلغه فهم، فمن أحب تقدير كلام الرب بذلك فهو مغفل. وكذلك فعله تعالى خارج عن وصف فعل الخلق. وفي ثبوت المخالفة من جميع الوجوه نفي الحدثية؛ لما به يقع الوفاق، وبطل معنى الأعراض والتفرق والاجتماع والحد والغاية والزيادة والنقصان؛ إذ ذلك وصف كلام الخلق، والله الموفق.
In the witnessed world, by it humans are distinguished from other animals, even though every [animal] possesses the potential for sound. So [human speech] is either due to inability to speak or due to silence. Then it cannot be free from being [produced] in imitation of the speech of another, in which case there is similarity [between them]. And His statement 'There is nothing like unto Him' (42:11) indicates the negation of similarity to Him in attribute and essence. And His statement 'They created like His creation' (13:16) supports that similarity of action necessitates similarity, along with the statement that if all of creation gathered they could not produce its like, so similarity is negated. For in it [i.e., created speech] there is likeness. So His opposition to all the speech of creation is established, as established for His essence, [and] despite the fact that not all the speech of creation has been tested to grasp the extent of its meanings. And He has mentioned the speech of the ant, the hoopoe, the glorification of the mountains, and other things, none of which is understood by alphabetic letters nor according to the understood [pattern] of human speech. And since it is established that there is some speech whose measure does not reach the capacity of creation nor does understanding reach it, whoever wishes to measure the speech of the Lord by that is foolish. Likewise, His action, exalted is He, is outside the description of the action of creation. And in the establishment of opposition from all aspects lies the negation of temporality; because by it agreement occurs, and the meaning of accidents, separation, composition, limit, end, increase, and decrease becomes invalid—since that is the description of the speech of creation. And God is the Giver of success.
Source pages p. 657

Commentary
This passage defines the radical difference between God's speech and created speech. It begins by noting that in the witnessed world, speech distinguishes humans from animals, yet even animals have potential for sound. The author then argues that if human speech imitates another's speech, it implies similarity; but God's statement 'There is nothing like unto Him' negates any similarity in attribute and essence. Another verse, 'They created like His creation,' shows that similarity in action would imply similarity, but the inimitability of the Qur'an proves its uniqueness. The argument proceeds: since creation cannot produce the like of God's speech, similarity is negated. The author points out that not all created speech has been examined to its full extent, and that God mentions the speech of the ant, hoopoe, and mountains—none of which conforms to human letters or understanding. Therefore, measuring divine speech by human standards is foolish. Finally, the author concludes that this total opposition to created speech negates temporality (hadath) and eliminates attributes like accidents, separation, composition, limit, etc., which characterize created speech.

Key Terms
الكلام
الشبه
المخالفة
الحدثية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think God's speech is like human speech, just more perfect.
Correction: The passage emphasizes that God's speech is entirely different in kind, not just in degree.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, what is the purpose of mentioning the speech of the ant, hoopoe, and mountains?
A) To show that animals can speak human languages
B) To demonstrate that God's speech is understood through letters
C) To prove that some speech is not composed of human letters and is beyond human understanding
D) To argue that all speech is created

Key Takeaway
God's speech is completely unlike any created speech, and therefore it is eternal and not subject to temporal attributes.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite the Quran, do you ever unconsciously judge its eloquence or meaning by human literary standards? This lesson says anyone who measures the speech of the Lord by that is foolish. Will you repent of that hidden arrogance and approach the Quran as truly incomparable starting today?
?
The passage mentions speech of ants and mountains that we cannot fathom. How often do you reduce God's actions and words to what you can understand? In what specific area of your life do you need to submit to the mystery of God's speech without demanding it fit your logic?
?
If God's speech is totally other, then every time you read the Quran you are encountering something beyond this world. Does that make you tremble with awe? Or have you become numb from familiarity? What one change will you make to restore the reverence that this truth demands?

Proof that God's Speech is Essential
Maturidi proves that God's speech is essential via disjunctive argument.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi uses a logical disjunction to prove that God's attribute of speech is essential to His essence, not a separate accidental attribute.

Core Idea
God's speech is not other than Him, otherwise it would be a sign of need.

Imam Maturidi now presents a concise logical argument to settle the question of whether God's speech is something separate from His essence or identical with it. He sets up a disjunction—two mutually exclusive possibilities—and shows that only one leads to a coherent understanding of divine perfection. This passage is a clear example of how kalam reasoning proceeds in matters of divine attributes.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic and English text side by side, noticing the structure of the argument.
Pay attention to the phrase 'لا يخلو من أن يكون غيره أو ليس غيره'.
2
Identify the disjunction
Notice the two possibilities: either speech is other than God, or it is not. The passage uses a logical 'either-or' structure.
3
Trace the consequence of each branch
For the first branch, understand that being 'other' implies need and temporality. For the second, conclude that God is speaking by essence.
The first branch leads to a defect, the second to perfection.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
The argument shows that speech is essential, not accidental, and thus eternal and perfect, consistent with God's nature.
This conclusion safeguards divine transcendence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم لا يخلو من أن يكون غيره فيزول عنه ما ذكرنا من الآفة بغيره ، وذلك علم الحاجة وأمارة الحدث، أو ليس غيره فيكون بنفسه متكلما قادرا عالما. وبالله التوفيق.
Then it cannot be free from either being other than Him, in which case the defect we mentioned would depart from it [i.e., speech] due to it being other [than Him]—and that is a sign of need and a marker of temporality—or it is not other than Him, in which case He is by His essence speaking, powerful, knowing. And with God is success.
Source pages p. 657

Commentary
This passage is a concise logical proof that God's attribute of speech is essential, not accidental. It presents a disjunction: either the speech is other than God, or it is not other than Him. If it were other than Him, then the defect (i.e., need and imperfection) would be removed from it because it is other; but being other implies need and temporality (hadath). If it is not other than Him, then God is by His very essence speaking (mutakallim), powerful, and knowing. The conclusion is that the speech is essential to His essence, not a separate created thing.

Key Terms
غيره
الآفة
الحدث
بذاته

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does Maturidi conclude if God's speech were other than His essence?
A) It would be eternal
B) It would be a sign of need and temporality
C) It would be identical to human speech
D) It would be permissible to call it created

Key Takeaway
God's speech is not separate from His essence; to claim otherwise would imply need and temporality, which are impossible for God.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you truly believe that God's speech is essential to Him—not a created thing—how would that change the way you approach reading the Qur'an today? Will you read it as if every word is directly from His essence, and what will you do differently in your next recitation to honor that?
?
Think of one attribute of God that you sometimes treat as if it is separate from Him (for example, His mercy or His justice). How does this lesson's argument that an attribute cannot be 'other than Him' without implying need challenge your assumption? Will you recommit to believing that all His attributes are essential, and how will that affect your trust in Him this week?

Permissibility of Calling Heard Speech 'God's Speech'
Maturidi explains the metaphorical attribution of heard speech to God.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Maturidi permits calling the recited Qur'an 'God's speech' and how this attribution is metaphorical, not literal.

Core Idea
Heard speech is attributed to God by agreement, not by essence.

When Muslims recite the Qur'an, they say 'this is God's speech.' But how can a created sound be literally the speech of the eternal Creator? Maturidi addresses this by explaining that the attribution is metaphorical, based on agreement (muwāfaqa), similar to how we attribute letters or poems to their authors. In this passage, he lays out the rational proof for this view.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
First, read Maturidi's Arabic text and its English translation. Note the key term 'muwāfaqa' (agreement/metaphorical attribution).
This passage is dense; read slowly.
2
Identify the main claim
What exactly does Maturidi say is permissible? How does he qualify it? Pay attention to the phrase 'on the way of agreement'.
3
Understand the proof
Maturidi provides a proof based on the nature of the heard speech. Why can't it be literally God's speech? Focus on the impossibility of an accident being in two places.
An accident (ʿaraḍ) cannot exist in two loci at once.
4
Follow the analogies
Maturidi gives two analogies: one from human speech and one from divine attributes. How do these support his point?
The analogies show that what is perceived is a created representation of the original.
5
Reflect on the misconception
Consider the common misunderstanding that the recited Qur'an is literally God's essence or literal speech. How does Maturidi correct this?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويجوز القول - بما يسمع من الخلق كلام الله على الموافقة ، كما يقال في الرسائل والقصائد والأقاويل ، دليله أن ذلك خلق من الخلق ، ولا يحتمل أن يكون الله بذاته [ متكلما] ، مع ما لا يخلو أن يكون المسموع عرضا ، فمحال كونه في مكانين ، وكذلك الجسم أو لا هما ، فمحال كونه في مكان، المكان وعن ، فثبت أن وجه الإضافة إليه على ما ذكرنا ، مع ما يجوز أن يسمعنا بما ليس بكلامه كما أسمع كل منا الآخر كلامه وإن لم يكن ذلك بعينه كلامه ، وكما أعلمنا قدرته وعلمه وربوبيته بخلقه وإن لم يكن هو هو، يسمع الله كلامه وبالله التوفيق.
It is permissible to say—concerning what is heard from creation as the speech of God—by way of agreement [i.e., metaphorical attribution], just as one says in [the case of] letters, poems, and sayings. Its proof is that that is a creation from creation, and it is not possible that God be by His essence speaking [in such a way], with the consideration that what is heard cannot be free from being an accident—so its being in two places is impossible—and likewise a body or neither, so its being in a place is impossible. So it is established that the mode of attribution to Him is as we have mentioned. Additionally, it is permissible that He makes us hear what is not His speech, just as each of us makes another hear his speech although that [heard] is not exactly his speech; and just as He made us know His power, knowledge, and lordship through His creation although it is not Him [directly]. God makes hear His speech—and with God is success.
Source pages p. 657

Commentary
This passage addresses a potential objection: how can we call the audible recitation 'God's speech'? The author says it is permissible metaphorically, by agreement (muwāfaqa), as when one attributes a letter or poem to its author even though the physical text is a creation. The proof is that the heard sound is an accident, and accidents cannot exist in two places (i.e., cannot be both in God's essence and in the reciter). If it were a body or something else, location would be impossible. Therefore, the attribution is relational, not literal. The author adds that God can make us hear something that is not literally His speech, just as one person makes another hear his speech through a created medium, and just as God shows His attributes through creation.

Key Terms
الموافقة
العرض
الإضافة
الخلق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the recited Qur'an is literally God's essence or literal speech.
Correction: Maturidi explains it is attributed metaphorically by agreement, not literally as an accident in God's essence.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, why can't the heard speech be literally God's speech?
A) Because it is a body and bodies cannot be in two places
B) Because it is an accident and accidents cannot be in two places or in God's essence
C) Because it is created and cannot be attributed to God at all
D) Because God does not speak

Key Takeaway
Maturidi permits calling heard speech 'God's speech' only metaphorically, by agreement, not by essence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear the Qur'an recited, do you ever catch yourself venerating the sound itself rather than submitting to the meaning it conveys? What practical step can you take today to ensure your heart focuses on the divine message beyond the physical voice?
?
The passage compares hearing God's speech through recitation to knowing His power through creation. Does your appreciation of the Qur'an's beauty consistently lead you to greater awe of the Creator, or does it sometimes stop at aesthetic pleasure? How will you change that?
?
If the physical words you read are not God's essence, then what does that imply about your responsibility to live by those words? Are you more diligent in perfecting your recitation or in implementing its commands? Which deserves more of your effort right now?

Moses Hearing God's Uncreated Speech
Maturidi answers the objection about Moses hearing God's speech.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's response to the objection about Moses hearing God's speech, and how he distinguishes between the created medium and the uncreated speech itself.

Core Idea
Moses heard God's uncreated speech through created means.

A key objection in kalam concerns the verse 'And God spoke to Moses directly.' If God's speech is uncreated, how could Moses hear it? Maturidi answers by distinguishing the medium (created letters and sounds) from the speech itself (uncreated). This lesson unpacks that distinction.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and answer
Read the Arabic passage and translation to grasp the question and Maturidi's response.
Notice the clear structure: a conditional question followed by a direct answer.
2
Identify the key distinction
Maturidi distinguishes between the means of hearing (Moses' tongue, created letters and sound) and what is heard (uncreated speech). Trace this in the text.
This is a classic solution to the problem of how the uncreated can be perceived by creation.
3
Reflect on the theological implication
Consider why this distinction matters for the doctrine of God's speech. It upholds the uncreatedness of the Qur'an while explaining how Moses heard it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قال قائل : هل أسمع الله كلامه حيث قال : وكلم الله موسى تكليما ، قيل : أسمعه بلسان موسى و بحروف خلقها وصوت أنشأه ، فهو أسمعه ما ليس بمخلوق . والقول بالوقف يخرج على وجهين: أحدهما أن يقال : ليس هو الله ولا غيره ، فيكون وقفا عن علم ، وهو حق على ما ثبت في العلم والقدرة . والثاني : أن يكون لا يعلم أخلق أو غيره ، فإنه بعيد ؛ لما لا يخلو من أن يذهب مذهب التقليد ، وأكثر القوم على نفي ذلك ، بل أجمع على لزوم العلم أنه الخلق أو غيره ، فحق أو بعد ، فإنه لا يعدو من أن يعلم أنه بذاته متكلم ، فيكون بمعنى [ما] ذكرت أو لا بذاته ، فهو غيره ، وكل الأغيار الله خلق [على] ما روى فيه سمع أو لا ، ثبت أن القول بالغيرية لله يوجب الحدث، والحدث والخلق إذ هو منه أو لا ، يعلم أنه بذاته متكلم أو لا، فيكون الوقف وقفا للجهل مثله التعلم؛ لأنه لا دليل دفعه إلى ذلك القول ليتكلم فيه ، إنما هو الجهل : أو أن يكون الوقف بما لا يعلم مراد السائل فيه أنه ما يعنى بكلام الله والقرآن : أهو هذا المتبعض المتجزئ، أو الذي لا يوصف بشيء من ذلك؟ وذلك على الوصف الذي بينا فهو حق أن لا يجيب لأحد يسأله عن كلام متوجه حتى يعلم ما يريد به ، والله أعلم .
If someone says: Did God make hear His speech when He said 'And God spoke to Moses directly' (4:164)? The answer: He made him hear through the tongue of Moses and through letters He created and a sound He originated, so He made him hear what is not created. The position of waqf (suspension of judgment) appears in two ways: first, that one says 'It is neither God nor other than God,' which is a waqf based on knowledge, and it is correct according to what is established concerning knowledge and power. Second, that one does not know whether it is created or other, which is far-fetched, because it inevitably tends toward blind imitation, and most of the people deny that; rather, they are unanimous on the necessity of knowing whether it is created or other, so it is either correct or far-fetched. For one cannot escape knowing that He is by His essence speaking, so [the speech] is in the sense I mentioned, or [it is] not by His essence, so it is other than Him, and all other [than God] is God's creation—whether one has heard a report [about it] or not. It is established that the statement of otherness regarding God necessitates temporality, and temporality and being created, since it is from Him or not. One knows that He is by His essence speaking or not; thus the waqf becomes a waqf of ignorance, like learning? because there is no proof that pushes him to that statement to speak about it; it is only ignorance. Or [there is] the waqf due to not knowing the intention of the questioner in what he means by 'the speech of God' and 'the Qur'an'—whether it is this divisible and partitioned thing, or that which is not described by any of that? According to the description we have explained, it is correct not to answer anyone who asks about a matter of speech until one knows what he intends by it. And God knows best.
Source pages p. 658

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer regarding the verse about Moses hearing God's speech. The objector asks: Did God make Moses hear His speech? The answer distinguishes: God made him hear through created means (Moses' tongue, created letters and sound), so what Moses heard is not uncreated. The second part discusses the 'waqf' position (suspending judgment on whether the Qur'an is created or uncreated). Two forms are given: the first is a knowing suspension, i.e., saying it is neither God nor other, which is valid; the second is ignorance, which is rejected because one must know that God is speaking essentially. If speech is essential, it is uncreated; if not, it is created. Thus the waqf of ignorance is baseless. Alternatively, if the questioner is ambiguous about what he means by 'speech', one may suspend until clarification.

Key Terms
كلام
خلق
صوت
حروف

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that if Moses heard God's speech, then God's speech must be created because it entered creation.
Correction: Maturidi shows that the medium (letters, sounds) is created, but the speech itself remains uncreated. Hearing does not necessitate the speech itself being created.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, what did Moses hear that is not created?
A) The letters and sound
B) The speech of God
C) The tongue of Moses
D) The voice of an angel

Key Takeaway
Maturidi defends the uncreatedness of God's speech by arguing that Moses heard it through created means.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite the Qur'an, do you treat the words as mere sounds and letters, or as the very uncreated speech of God that reaches you through created means? What would change in your recitation if you truly internalized that these sounds carry the Eternal's word?
?
Moses heard God's speech directly, though through created mediums. You have the Qur'an as God's speech preserved. Are you listening to it with the same urgency and reverence as if you were hearing it from God Himself? If not, what is holding you back?
?
If every created sound and letter in the Qur'an is a vessel for the uncreated, how does that demand a change in your attitude when you read or listen to it? Will you commit to reciting the next verse with the awareness that you are encountering the Divine?

The Two Types of Waqf on the Qur'an
Maturidi discusses the waqf position and its two forms.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two types of waqf (suspending judgment) regarding whether the Qur'an is created, and why Maturidi accepts the first but rejects the second.

Core Idea
Not all waqf is valid; only a knowing suspension is acceptable.

Maturidi now turns to the position of waqf, which some adopt to avoid taking a stance on whether the Qur'an is created. He identifies two forms: one based on knowledge, which is correct, and one based on ignorance, which is rejected. This lesson unpacks that distinction and its rationale.

Guided Path
1
Enumerate the two types of waqf
Read the passage and find the two categories: knowing waqf (saying 'neither God nor other') and ignorant waqf (not knowing whether created or other).
The knowing waqf is described as 'correct' based on knowledge and power.
2
Understand why the second waqf is rejected
Maturidi argues that this waqf leads to blind imitation and denies the necessity of knowing that God speaks essentially. If God speaks essentially, His speech is uncreated; if not, it is created. Ignorance here is not excusable.
3
Consider the third scenario: waqf due to ambiguity
Maturidi mentions another valid reason for waqf: if the questioner's intent is unclear (what does he mean by 'speech'? the divisible Qur'an or the attribute?), then suspending judgment is correct until clarification.
This is a distinct case from the ignorant waqf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قال قائل : هل أسمع الله كلامه حيث قال : وكلم الله موسى تكليما ، قيل : أسمعه بلسان موسى و بحروف خلقها وصوت أنشأه ، فهو أسمعه ما ليس بمخلوق . والقول بالوقف يخرج على وجهين: أحدهما أن يقال : ليس هو الله ولا غيره ، فيكون وقفا عن علم ، وهو حق على ما ثبت في العلم والقدرة . والثاني : أن يكون لا يعلم أخلق أو غيره ، فإنه بعيد ؛ لما لا يخلو من أن يذهب مذهب التقليد ، وأكثر القوم على نفي ذلك ، بل أجمع على لزوم العلم أنه الخلق أو غيره ، فحق أو بعد ، فإنه لا يعدو من أن يعلم أنه بذاته متكلم ، فيكون بمعنى [ما] ذكرت أو لا بذاته ، فهو غيره ، وكل الأغيار الله خلق [على] ما روى فيه سمع أو لا ، ثبت أن القول بالغيرية لله يوجب الحدث، والحدث والخلق إذ هو منه أو لا ، يعلم أنه بذاته متكلم أو لا، فيكون الوقف وقفا للجهل مثله التعلم؛ لأنه لا دليل دفعه إلى ذلك القول ليتكلم فيه ، إنما هو الجهل : أو أن يكون الوقف بما لا يعلم مراد السائل فيه أنه ما يعنى بكلام الله والقرآن : أهو هذا المتبعض المتجزئ، أو الذي لا يوصف بشيء من ذلك؟ وذلك على الوصف الذي بينا فهو حق أن لا يجيب لأحد يسأله عن كلام متوجه حتى يعلم ما يريد به ، والله أعلم .
If someone says: Did God make hear His speech when He said 'And God spoke to Moses directly' (4:164)? The answer: He made him hear through the tongue of Moses and through letters He created and a sound He originated, so He made him hear what is not created. The position of waqf (suspension of judgment) appears in two ways: first, that one says 'It is neither God nor other than God,' which is a waqf based on knowledge, and it is correct according to what is established concerning knowledge and power. Second, that one does not know whether it is created or other, which is far-fetched, because it inevitably tends toward blind imitation, and most of the people deny that; rather, they are unanimous on the necessity of knowing whether it is created or other, so it is either correct or far-fetched. For one cannot escape knowing that He is by His essence speaking, so [the speech] is in the sense I mentioned, or [it is] not by His essence, so it is other than Him, and all other [than God] is God's creation—whether one has heard a report [about it] or not. It is established that the statement of otherness regarding God necessitates temporality, and temporality and being created, since it is from Him or not. One knows that He is by His essence speaking or not; thus the waqf becomes a waqf of ignorance, like learning? because there is no proof that pushes him to that statement to speak about it; it is only ignorance. Or [there is] the waqf due to not knowing the intention of the questioner in what he means by 'the speech of God' and 'the Qur'an'—whether it is this divisible and partitioned thing, or that which is not described by any of that? According to the description we have explained, it is correct not to answer anyone who asks about a matter of speech until one knows what he intends by it. And God knows best.

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer regarding the verse about Moses hearing God's speech. The objector asks: Did God make Moses hear His speech? The answer distinguishes: God made him hear through created means (Moses' tongue, created letters and sound), so what Moses heard is not uncreated. Correction: Maturidi shows that only a knowing waqf is valid; an ignorant waqf is blameworthy because the matter is knowable and avoiding knowledge can lead to blind imitation.

God's Speech is Uncreated and the Two Types of Suspension of Judgment
Maturidi discusses God's speech, its uncreatedness, and the waqf position.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi argues that God's speech is uncreated yet can be heard through created means, and how he distinguishes between valid and invalid forms of suspending judgment (waqf) regarding its nature.

Core Idea
God's speech is uncreated; only the medium of hearing is created.

In this passage, Imam Maturidi tackles a central theological question: How can the Quran be both the eternal speech of God and yet be heard in temporal, created words? He presents a nuanced argument that preserves the uncreatedness of divine speech while explaining how it is communicated to prophets. He then clarifies the two types of suspension of judgment (waqf) that some adopt, showing which is valid and which is not.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing it, then read the translation. Let the author's own argument come through before you interpret.
Notice Maturidi's concise style and the logical flow from one point to the next.
2
Identify the two waqf positions
Locate where Maturidi describes the two types of suspension of judgment. Note the difference between the first (valid) and the second (invalid) and the reasons given.
The first type is based on knowledge; the second is based on ignorance and leads to blind imitation.
3
Reflect on the Moses example
Consider how Maturidi uses the story of Moses (peace be upon him) to illustrate that God's speech can be heard through created letters and sound, yet what is heard is uncreated.
This example is key to understanding how the uncreated speech relates to created mediums.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يكون الله بذاته متكلما، مع ما لا يخلو أن يكون المسموع عرضا، فمحال كونه في مكانين، وكذلك الجسم أو لا هما، فمحال كونه في مكان، فثبت أن وجه الإضافة إليه على ما ذكرنا، مع ما يجوز أن يسمعنا بما ليس بكلامه كما أسمع كل منا الآخر كلامه وإن لم يكن ذلك بعينه كلامه، وكما أعلمنا قدرته وعلمه وربوبيته بخلقه وإن لم يكن هو هو، يسمع الله كلامه. وبالله التوفيق.

فإن قال قائل: هل أسمع الله كلامه حيث قال: {وكلم الله موسى تكليما}؟ قيل: أسمعه بلسان موسى وبحروف خلقها وصوت أنشأه، فهو أسمعه ما ليس بمخلوق. والقول بالوقف يخرج على وجهين: أحدهما أن يقال: ليس هو الله ولا غيره، فيكون وقفا عن علم، وهو حق على ما ثبت في العلم والقدرة. والثاني: أن يكون لا يعلم أخلق غيره، فإنه بعيد؛ لما لا يخلو من أن يذهب مذهب التقليد، وأكثر القوم على نفي ذلك، بل أجمع على لزوم العلم أنه الخلق غيره.

جاء على هامش النص: أي لا عرضا ولا جسما.

وبعد، فإنه لا يعدو من أن يعلم أنه بذاته متكلم، فيكون بمعنى ما ذكرت أو لا بذاته، فهو غيره، وكل الأغيار الله خلق على ما روى فيه سمع أو لا، ثبت أن القول بالغيرية لله يوجب الحدث، والحدث والخلق إذ هو منه أو لا، يعلم أنه بذاته متكلم أو لا، فيكون الوقف وقفا للجهل مثله التعلم؛ لأنه لا دليل دفعه إلى ذلك القول ليتكلم فيه، إنما هو الجهل: أو أن يكون الوقف بما لا يعلم مراد السائل فيه أنه ما يعنى بكلام الله والقرآن: أهو هذا المتبعض المتجزئ، أو الذي لا يوصف بشيء من ذلك؟ وذلك على الوصف الذي بينا فهو حق أن لا يجيب لأحد يسأله عن كلام متوجه حتى يعلم ما يريد به، والله أعلم.
God is by His essence speaking, but since what is heard must be an accident, it is impossible for it to exist in two places, and likewise a body or both, so it is impossible for it to exist in a place. Thus it is established that the mode of attribution to Him is as we have mentioned, together with the possibility that He makes us hear what is not His speech just as He made each one of us hear the speech of another even though that is not exactly his speech, and just as He made us know His power, knowledge, and lordship through His creation even though creation is not He Himself. [Thus] God makes [one] hear His speech. And with Allah is success.

If a questioner says: Did God make Moses hear His speech when He said, 'And God spoke to Moses with speech'? It is said: He made him hear it through the tongue of Moses and through letters which He created and a sound which He produced, so He made him hear that which is not created. The position of suspending judgment (waqf) emerges in two ways: One is to say: 'It is not God nor other than Him,' and that is a suspension out of knowledge, and it is true based on what is established regarding knowledge and power. The second is that one does not know whether it is created or other than Him; that is far [from correct], because it cannot avoid following blind imitation, and most of the [scholarly] community reject that; rather there is consensus on the necessity of knowing that it is created, other than Him.

Marginal note: i.e., not an accident and not a body.

Moreover, [the issue] does not go beyond either knowing that He is speaking by His essence, so it is in the sense I mentioned, or not by His essence, so it is other than Him. And everything other than God is created, based on what is transmitted regarding hearing or not, it is established that affirming otherness (ghayriyya) for God necessitates originatedness (hadath), and originatedness and creation are from Him or not. One knows that He is speaking by His essence or not, so the suspension becomes a suspension of ignorance like learning; because there is no evidence that drives one to that statement to speak therein; rather it is ignorance. Or the suspension is because one does not know the intent of the questioner regarding what is meant by 'God's speech' and the Qur'an: whether it is this divisible and partitionable [thing] or that which is not described by any of that? And that is based on the description we have clarified, so it is correct not to answer anyone who asks about speech in general until one knows what he intends by it. And God knows best.
Source pages p. 658

Commentary
This passage is a theological argument about God's attribute of speech (kalam). It begins by stating that God is by His essence speaking, but what is heard (the recited Quran) is an accident, which cannot exist in two places or be a body, so it cannot be God's essence. Then it explains that God can make us hear His speech through created means: He made Moses hear His speech through the tongue of Moses and created letters and sound, yet what Moses heard was not created—it was God's uncreated speech. The passage then discusses the two ways of suspending judgment (waqf) about the nature of the Quran: the first is to say it is neither God nor other than Him, which is a suspension based on knowledge and is valid; the second is to claim ignorance of whether it is created or uncreated, which is rejected because it leads to blind imitation and the consensus is that it is created (i.e., the letters and sounds are created, but the speech itself is not). A marginal note clarifies that 'by His essence' means not an accident or body. Then the author explains that affirming otherness (ghayriyya) for God would entail that His speech is originated, which is impossible. Finally, he advises that one should not answer a question about kalam until the questioner's intent is clear—whether they mean the divisible Quran or the indivisible attribute of God.

Key Terms
متكلماً
عرض
وقف
خلق الحروف
غيرية
حدوث

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that because the Quran is heard in created letters and sounds, it is itself created.
Correction: The passage clarifies that God's speech is uncreated; only the medium (letters, sounds) is created. What Moses heard was uncreated speech through created means.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the first valid type of suspension of judgment (waqf) regarding God's speech?
A) Saying 'It is not God nor other than Him' based on knowledge.
B) Saying 'I do not know whether it is created or not' out of ignorance.
C) Saying 'It is created' because it is heard through created letters.
D) Saying 'It is uncreated' because it is God's speech.

Key Takeaway
God's speech is uncreated; it is heard through created means, and valid suspension of judgment about its nature is based on knowledge, not ignorance.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite the Quran, do you ever stop to consider that you are hearing the uncreated speech of God through created sounds? How does this truth change the way you approach the Quran?
?
The passage warns against a suspension of judgment based on ignorance and blind imitation. Are there areas in your faith where you have passively accepted claims without seeking knowledge? What would it cost you to investigate them?
?
God made Moses hear His speech through created means. Have you ever felt that God's speech (the Quran) speaks directly to your heart despite being delivered through human words? How could you become more attentive to that reality?

The Three Divisions of Allah's Names
Maturidi classifies divine names into three linguistic categories.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's classification of the divine names into three linguistic categories: names that are distinct, names that refer to the essence, and names derived from attributes.

Core Idea
Allah's names are not all the same; they fall into three linguistic categories.

Imam Maturidi provides a systematic classification of the names of Allah based on their linguistic meaning. This classification helps us understand how different names relate to Allah's essence and actions. In this passage, he explains three distinct types of divine names.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage with translation
Begin by reading the Arabic passage and its literal translation. Notice the threefold division indicated by 'قسم' and 'الثاني' and 'الثالث'. Pay attention to how Maturidi introduces each category.
The passage is continuous but has clear markers for each division.
2
Analyze the first category: names that are 'aghyār'
The first division consists of names like 'Alīm and Qadīr, which are different from each other. Maturidi explains that these names are based on created things (e.g., mercy, Paradise). They do not imply that Allah acquired a new attribute through creation.
3
Understand the second and third categories
The second category includes names that refer directly to Allah's essence, such as al-Wāḥid, Allāh, al-Raḥmān. The third category consists of names derived from attributes, like al-ʿĀlim, al-Qādir. Note that the third category is incomplete in the text.
The passage breaks off, but the intended classification is clear.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة في أسماء الله عز وجل] قال أبو منصور رحمه الله : القول فى أسماء الله عز وجل عندنا / على أقسام في مفهوم اللغة : قسم منها إلى تسميتنا له بها ، وهن أغيار ؛ لأن قولنا عليم يرجع غير قولنا قدير ، وعلى هذا المروى إن لله تعالى كذا وكذا اسما ، وذلك نحو ما ذكر من خلق كذا وكذا رحمة ، لا أنه كان رحيما بتلك الرحمة المخلوقة؛ إذ لا يحتمل أن يكون في أول خلقه غير رحيم، أو كان كذلك غير رحيم حتى خلق تلك الرحمة وجعل واحدة بين خلقه ، ولكن بما كانت برحمته سميت به ، وكذلك اسم الجنة والمطر وعلى ذلك قيل في العبارات : هى أمره ، وإنما كانت به ، لا أنها هو ، ومثله يتكلم بعلمه وقدرته على إرادة معلومه ومقدوره ؛ إذ ذلك سببه ، فمثله الأول مشعره ، ولا قوة إلا بالله والثاني يرجع ، معناه إلى ذاته مما عجز الخلق عن الوقوف على مراد ذاته إلا به ، وإن كان يتعالى عن الحروف التي بها يفهم ، وذلك أيضا يختلف باختلاف الألسن على إرادة حقيقة ذاته به ، وذلك نحو الواحد ، الله ، الرحمن ، الموجود ، والقديم ، والمعبود ، والمعبود ، ونحو ذلك والثالث يرجع إلى الاشتقاق عن الصفات من نحو العالم القادر ، مما لو كانت 1
Question concerning the names of Allah, Mighty and Majestic. Abu Mansur (may Allah have mercy on him) said: The statement concerning the names of Allah, Mighty and Majestic – with us – is according to divisions in the linguistic understanding: A division: to our naming Him with them, and they are different (aghyār); because our saying ‘Alīm (Knowing) refers to other than our saying Qadīr (Powerful). And upon this is the transmitted report that Allah, exalted, has such-and-such names. That is like what was mentioned of the creation of such-and-such mercy, not that He was Merciful by that created mercy; for it is not possible that He was in the beginning of His creation other than Merciful, or that He was similarly other than Merciful until He created that mercy and made one among His creation; but because it was by His mercy, it was named by it, and likewise the name of Paradise and rain. And upon that it was said in expressions: they are His command, and they were only by Him, not that they are He. And likewise one speaks by His knowledge and His power concerning the will of what He knows and what He is capable of; for that is its cause. So its like, the first, is an indicator of Him. And there is no power except with Allah. The second returns, its meaning to His essence (dhāt), which the creation is unable to comprehend the meaning of His essence except by it, even though He is exalted above the letters by which it is understood. That also differs according to the diversity of languages regarding intending the reality of His essence by it. That is like: al-Wāḥid (the One), Allāh, al-Raḥmān (the Merciful), al-Mawjūd (the Existent), al-Qadīm (the Eternal), al-Maʿbūd (the Worshipped), al-Maʿbūd (the Worshipped), and the like. And the third returns to derivation (ishtiqāq) from the attributes, such as al-ʿĀlim (the Knowing), al-Qādir (the Powerful), from which if they were...
Source pages p. 664

Commentary
This passage classifies the names of Allah into three linguistic categories. The first category consists of names we attribute to Him that are distinct (aghyār) from one another, such as 'Alīm and Qadīr – each refers to a different meaning. These are the names traditionally reported (e.g., 'Allah has 99 names'). Maturidi explains that such names do not imply that Allah became merciful by a created mercy; rather, because He created mercy, He is called Merciful. Similarly, names like 'Paradise' and 'rain' are derived from His creation. The second category includes names that refer to His essence (dhāt) – such as al-Wāḥid, Allāh, al-Raḥmān, al-Mawjūd, al-Qadīm, al-Maʿbūd. Creation cannot comprehend His essence except through these names, and they transcend specific letters, varying across languages. The third category consists of names derived (ishtiqāq) from attributes, like al-ʿĀlim and al-Qādir. The passage breaks off mid-sentence, but the intended point likely concerns the relationship between such derived names and the eternal attributes.

Key Terms
أغيار
أسماء
ذات
اشتقاق
صفات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All of Allah's names are direct descriptions of His essence in the same way.
Correction: Maturidi clarifies that some names (like al-Raḥīm) are derived from His acts (creating mercy), not directly from His essence.

Checkpoint
Which of the following is an example of the first category of names (those that are 'aghyār' and based on created things)?
A) al-Wāḥid
B) al-Qadīr
C) al-Raḥmān
D) al-Mawjūd

Key Takeaway
Maturidi classifies divine names into three linguistic categories: names based on acts (aghyār), names referring to the essence, and names derived from attributes.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you call upon Allah by name, which category do you most often use? How does this lesson challenge you to be more mindful of the meaning behind each name in your worship?
?
If names like 'al-Mawjūd' point directly to His essence, yet you cannot fully comprehend that essence, how does this affect the way you approach knowledge of Allah? What should you do with the names you cannot fully grasp?
?
The first category includes names like 'ar-Raheem' that come from His acts. When you experience mercy in your life, do you trace it back to Allah's eternal mercy, or do you focus only on the created means? How can this lesson deepen your gratitude and reliance on Him?

The First Division: Names from Created Things
Maturidi explains the first division: names that are other than the essence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's first division of Allah's names, which are derived from created things and are other than His essence.

Core Idea
Some of Allah's names refer to created manifestations, not His essence.

Imam Maturidi begins his classification by distinguishing names that we use for Allah but that actually refer to created entities, like mercy, paradise, or rain. This division emphasizes that these names are not identical with Allah's essence but are attributed to Him because they originate from Him, preserving His transcendence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on the first division
Read the Arabic text and translation for the first category of Allah's names according to Maturidi.
This category is the most detailed in the passage.
2
Identify the key concept
Notice that Maturidi says these names are 'other' (أغيار) than His essence, and they are derived from created things like mercy.
Example: 'All-Knowing' is a different name from 'All-Powerful'.
3
Reflect on the implications
Think about why Maturidi makes this distinction: to avoid anthropomorphism and to preserve God's transcendence.
This prevents people from thinking Allah's attributes are created.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة في أسماء الله عز وجل] قال أبو منصور رحمه الله : القول فى أسماء الله عز وجل عندنا / على أقسام في مفهوم اللغة : قسم منها إلى تسميتنا له بها، وهن أغيار؛ لأن قولنا عليم يرجع غير قولنا قدير، وعلى هذا المروى إن لله تعالى كذا وكذا اسما، وذلك نحو ما ذكر من خلق كذا وكذا رحمة، لا أنه كان رحيما بتلك الرحمة المخلوقة؛ إذ لا يحتمل أن يكون في أول خلقه غير رحيم، أو كان كذلك غير رحيم حتى خلق تلك الرحمة وجعل واحدة بين خلقه، ولكن بما كانت برحمته سميت به، وكذلك اسم الجنة والمطر وعلى ذلك قيل في العبارات : هي أمره، وإنما كانت به، لا أنها هو، ومثله يتكلم بعلمه وقدرته على إرادة معلومه ومقدوره؛ إذ ذلك سببه، فمثله الأول مشعره، ولا قوة إلا بالله والثاني يرجع معناه إلى ذاته مما عجز الخلق عن الوقوف على مراد ذاته إلا به، وإن كان يتعالى عن الحروف التي بها يفهم، وذلك أيضا يختلف باختلاف الألسن على إرادة حقيقة ذاته به، وذلك نحو الواحد، الله، الرحمن، الموجود، والقديم، والمعبود، والمعبود، ونحو ذلك والثالث يرجع إلى الاشتقاق عن الصفات من نحو العالم القادر، مما لو كانت في التحقيق غيره لاحتمل التبديل، ولصارت التسمية على غير تحقيق المعنى والمفهوم، ولجازت تسميته بكل ما يسمى غيره إذا لم يرد تحقيق المفهوم من معناه ولا قوة إلا بالله
Section on the names of Allah, may He be glorified and exalted. Abu Mansur, may Allah have mercy on him, said: The statement concerning the names of Allah, may He be glorified and exalted, according to us, is divided into categories in terms of linguistic concept: A category is that of our naming Him with them, and they are other [than His essence]; because our saying 'All-Knowing' refers back to other than our saying 'All-Powerful'. And upon this is the reported [hadith] that Allah Almighty has such-and-such names, such as what was mentioned of the creation of such-and-such mercy, not that He was Merciful with that created mercy; for it is not possible that He was in the beginning of His creation other than Merciful, or that He was not Merciful until He created that mercy and made one [part] among His creation, but because [things] are with His mercy they are named by it. Likewise the name 'Paradise' and 'rain'. And upon that it is said in expressions: they are His command, and they are only by Him, not that they are He. And similarly He speaks by His knowledge and His power upon the will of His known and His empowered; for that is its cause, so its example is the first indication. And there is no power except by Allah. The second returns in its meaning to His essence, from what the creation is incapable of grasping the intended meaning of His essence except by it, even though He is exalted above the letters by which it is understood. And that also differs according to different tongues upon intending the reality of His essence by it. That includes: al-Wahid (the One), Allah, al-Rahman (the All-Merciful), al-Mawjud (the Existing), al-Qadim (the Eternal), al-Ma'bub (the Worshipped), and al-Ma'bub, and similar to that. The third returns to derivation from attributes, such as al-Alim (the All-Knowing), al-Qadir (the All-Powerful). Because if they were in reality other than Him, change would be possible, and naming would become based on an unreal meaning and concept, and it would be permissible to name Him with everything by which others are named if the realization of the concept from its meaning is not intended. And there is no power except by Allah.
Source pages p. 664

Commentary
This passage is a classification of the names of Allah (أسماء الله) according to Imam Maturidi. He states that the discourse on Allah's names is divided into categories (أقسام) based on linguistic concept (مفهوم اللغة). He then enumerates three divisions:
1. The first division: Names that we use to address Him, which are other than His essence (أغيار). For example, the name 'All-Knowing' (عليم) is not the same as 'All-Powerful' (قدير); each refers to a different attribute. Maturidi explains that such names are derived from created things (like mercy created in the world) not that Allah's mercy is created; rather, He is eternally merciful. The name 'Paradise' or 'rain' are called His mercy, but they are not His essence. He also says that Allah speaks through His knowledge and power, which are causes of His acts.
2. The second division: Names that refer to His essence (ذاته), such as al-Wahid (the One), Allah, al-Rahman, etc. These names are such that creation cannot grasp the intended meaning except through these words, though Allah is exalted above letters. They vary by language but intend the reality of His essence.
3. The third division: Names derived from attributes (مشتقة عن الصفات), like al-Alim, al-Qadir. Maturidi argues that if these names were in reality other than Allah (i.e., created), they would be subject to change, and it would become permissible to name Him with any name of creation, which is not allowed. So these names must be based on real attributes.

Key Terms
أسماء الله
أقسام
تسمية
اغيار
رحمة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That all of Allah's names are created or that His attributes are created.
Correction: Maturidi clarifies that some names refer to created things, but they are not His essence; He is eternally merciful without needing a created mercy.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, why is the name 'Merciful' not derived from created mercy?
A) Because created mercy does not exist
B) Because He was always Merciful even before creating mercy
C) Because mercy is not a name of Allah
D) Because the name 'Merciful' refers to His essence

Key Takeaway
The first division shows that some of Allah's names are derived from created things and are other than His essence, preserving His transcendence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that Allah's mercy is not like the mercy you experience from any human being? When you say 'Ya Rahman,' are you aware that His mercy is eternal and not dependent on any created act? How does that affect the way you hope in His mercy, especially when you feel undeserving?
?
This lesson shows that some names of Allah come from created things like rain and paradise. Have you ever mistakenly thought of Allah's attributes as being similar to human qualities? What specific names do you need to purify your understanding of, so that you exalt Him above any likeness?
?
The passage says it is impossible for Allah to have been without mercy before creation. Do you live as if His mercy is always present, even when you cannot see it? When you face trials, do you forget that His mercy preceded your existence? What would change in your life if you fully internalized that His mercy is not created or conditional?

The Second Division: Names of Essence
Maturidi defines the second division: names that refer to the essence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's second division of Allah's names, which refer directly to His essence and are beyond full human comprehension.

Core Idea
Some of Allah's names directly signify His essence and are known only through revelation.

After discussing names derived from created things, Maturidi introduces a second category: names that return in meaning to Allah's essence itself. These names, such as al-Wahid (the One) and Allah, convey the reality of His essence, though the full understanding is beyond creation. This division highlights that while we use these names, their true meaning is grasped only through divine disclosure.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on the second division
Read the Arabic and translation for the second category.
This category is shorter but profound.
2
Identify the list of names
Note the names Maturidi includes: al-Wahid, Allah, al-Rahman, al-Mawjud, al-Qadim, al-Ma'bub.
These are not derived from any created thing.
3
Reflect on the meaning
Consider why Maturidi says creation cannot grasp the intended meaning except by these words, and that they differ by language.
This affirms the transcendence of Allah's essence.

The Third Division: Names from Attributes
Maturidi explains the third division: names derived from attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's third division of Allah's names, which are derived from His attributes and must be real, not metaphorical.

Core Idea
Names like 'All-Knowing' and 'All-Powerful' are derived from real attributes that are not created.

Maturidi concludes his classification with names that are derived from attributes, such as al-Alim (the All-Knowing) and al-Qadir (the All-Powerful). He argues that if these names were not based on real attributes inherent in the essence, they would be subject to change and would imply that any name could be used for Allah, which is false. Therefore, these names indicate real, uncreated attributes.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on the third division
Read the Arabic and translation for the third category.
This is the final category.
2
Understand the derivation
Notice that these names are derived from active attributes like knowledge and power.
They are not a separate essence.
3
Grasp the argument
Maturidi gives a hypothetical: if these names were other than His essence, they would be changeable, and any name could be used for Allah. This impossibility proves they are real.
This supports the reality of attributes.

Source Text

مسألة في أسماء الله عز وجل] قال أبو منصور رحمه الله : القول فى أسماء الله عز وجل عندنا / على أقسام في مفهوم اللغة : قسم منها إلى تسميتنا له بها، وهن أغيار؛ لأن قولنا عليم يرجع غير قولنا قدير، وعلى هذا المروى إن لله تعالى كذا وكذا اسما، وذلك نحو ما ذكر من خلق كذا وكذا رحمة، لا أنه كان رحيما بتلك الرحمة المخلوقة؛ إذ لا يحتمل أن يكون في أول خلقه غير رحيم، أو كان كذلك غير رحيم حتى خلق تلك الرحمة وجعل واحدة بين خلقه، ولكن بما كانت برحمته سميت به، وكذلك اسم الجنة والمطر وعلى ذلك قيل في العبارات : هي أمره، وإنما كانت به، لا أنها هو، ومثله يتكلم بعلمه وقدرته على إرادة معلومه ومقدوره؛ إذ ذلك سببه، فمثله الأول مشعره، ولا قوة إلا بالله والثاني يرجع معناه إلى ذاته مما عجز الخلق عن الوقوف على مراد ذاته إلا به، وإن كان يتعالى عن الحروف التي بها يفهم، وذلك أيضا يختلف باختلاف الألسن على إرادة حقيقة ذاته به، وذلك نحو الواحد، الله، الرحمن، الموجود، والقديم، والمعبود، والمعبود، ونحو ذلك والثالث يرجع إلى الاشتقاق عن الصفات من نحو العالم القادر، مما لو كانت في التحقيق غيره لاحتمل التبديل، ولصارت التسمية على غير تحقيق المعنى والمفهوم، ولجازت تسميته بكل ما يسمى غيره إذا لم يرد تحقيق المفهوم من معناه ولا قوة إلا بالله
Section on the names of Allah, may He be glorified and exalted. Abu Mansur, may Allah have mercy on him, said: The statement concerning the names of Allah, may He be glorified and exalted, according to us, is divided into categories in terms of linguistic concept: A category is that of our naming Him with them, and they are other [than His essence]; because our saying 'All-Knowing' refers back to other than our saying 'All-Powerful'. And upon this is the reported [hadith] that Allah Almighty has such-and-such names, such as what was mentioned of the creation of such-and-such mercy, not that He was Merciful with that created mercy; for it is not possible that He was in the beginning of His creation other than Merciful, or that He was not Merciful until He created that mercy and made one [part] among His creation, but because [things] are with His mercy they are named by it. Likewise the name 'Paradise' and 'rain'. And upon that it is said in expressions: they are His command, and they are only by Him, not that they are He. And similarly He speaks by His knowledge and His power upon the will of His known and His empowered; for that is its cause, so its example is the first indication. And there is no power except by Allah. The second returns in its meaning to His essence, from what the creation is incapable of grasping the intended meaning of His essence except by it, even though He is exalted above the letters by which it is understood. And that also differs according to different tongues upon intending the reality of His essence by it. That includes: al-Wahid (the One), Allah, al-Rahman (the All-Merciful), al-Mawjud (the Existing), al-Qadim (the Eternal), al-Ma'bub (the Worshipped), and al-Ma'bub, and similar to that. The third returns to derivation from attributes, such as al-Alim (the All-Knowing), al-Qadir (the All-Powerful). Because if they were in reality other than Him, change would be possible, and naming would become based on an unreal meaning and concept, and it would be permissible to name Him with everything by which others are named if the realization of the concept from its meaning is not intended. And there is no power except by Allah.
Source pages p. 664

Commentary
This passage is a classification of the names of Allah (أسماء الله) according to Imam Maturidi. He states that the discourse on Allah's names is divided into categories (أقسام) based on linguistic concept (مفهوم اللغة). He then enumerates three divisions:
1. The first division: Names that we use to address Him, which are other than His essence (أغيار). For example, the name 'All-Knowing' (عليم) is not the same as 'All-Powerful' (قدير); each refers to a different attribute. Maturidi explains that such names are derived from created things (like mercy created in the world) not that Allah's mercy is created; rather, He is eternally merciful. The name 'Paradise' or 'rain' are called His mercy, but they are not His essence. He also says that Allah speaks through His knowledge and power, which are causes of His acts.
2. The second division: Names that refer to His essence (ذاته), such as al-Wahid (the One), Allah, al-Rahman, etc. These names are such that creation cannot grasp the intended meaning except through these words, though Allah is exalted above letters. They vary by language but intend the reality of His essence.
3. The third division: Names derived from attributes (مشتقة عن الصفات), like al-Alim, al-Qadir. Maturidi argues that if these names were in reality other than Allah (i.e., created), they would be subject to change, and it would become permissible to name Him with any name of creation, which is not allowed. So these names must be based on real attributes.

Key Terms
اشتقاق
عالم
قادر
صفات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That Allah's attributes are created or separate from His essence.
Correction: Maturidi argues that if attributes were separate, change would be possible and naming would be arbitrary, which is not the case.

Checkpoint
What does Maturidi use to prove that names derived from attributes must be real?
A) The hadith about ninety-nine names
B) The argument that otherwise change and arbitrary naming would follow
C) The fact that these names are used in the Quran
D) The consensus of scholars

Key Takeaway
Names derived from attributes are based on real, uncreated attributes inherent in Allah's essence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you call upon Allah as al-Alim, do you truly believe that His knowledge is real and all-encompassing, or do you sometimes act as if He does not see you? How can you bring this reality into your daily choices?
?
If you have ever doubted that Allah's attributes are real and uncreated, what effect did that have on your certainty? What can you do today to strengthen your conviction that His names are not just empty labels?
?
Maturidi's argument shows that if Allah's names were mere metaphors, it would reduce Him to the level of creatures. Does your understanding of Allah's names reflect His majesty, or have you unknowingly diminished it? Commit to one specific way you will honor a divine name today.

The Dilemma of Pre-Eternal Knowledge
Maturidi refutes the claim that Allah's names are created by a logical dilemma.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the claim that Allah's names are created logically leads to attributing ignorance to Allah in pre-eternity, and how this corrupts tawhid.

Core Idea
Denying pre-eternal attributes forces a blasphemous implication of ignorance in Allah.

Imam Maturidi refutes those who say Allah's names are created by exposing the logical consequences for Allah's knowledge before creation. He presents a dilemma: either Allah knew His essence or He did not; each option forces an admission about the eternity of His names. This lesson unpacks that argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the full English translation. Notice the interrogative style used to expose the contradiction.
2
Identify the two options in the dilemma
Look for the conditional phrases: 'If He did not know it...' and 'If He knew it...'. Understand what each implies about Allah's knowledge.
The first option leads to ignorance, the second to eternal knowledge.
3
Trace the consequence for tawhid
See how Maturidi concludes that denying the name in pre-eternity corrupts tawhid, and then refutes Jahm's position.
The final part shows that if knowledge occurs after non-existence, the entire position collapses.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ما يُسأل من يجعل هذه الأسماء حادثة، ثم لا تحقق الله علما في الأزل إذ كيف كان أمره قبل الخلق، أكان يعلم ذاته أو ما يفعل أو لا ؟ وكذلك أكان يعلم ذاته شيئا أو لا يعلمها ؟ فإن كان لا يعلمها، فهو إذا جاهل حتى، أحدث العلم له فصار به عالما، وإن كان يعلمها عالما، وإن كان يعلمها، فإذا بعلم ذاته عالما أو لا ؟ " فإن ذاته عالما فلزم / القول بهذا الاسم فى الأزل، وفى غيرية الاسم فساد التوحيد والأصل على قول منكرى الصفات إذ لم يكن له هذا الاسم، ولم يكن له صفة هي علم يعلم ذاته فى الأزل يجب ما قاله جهم" ينفى الأسماء والصفات وحدثها فيكون غير عالم ولا قادر ثم عليم، جل الله عن ذلك وتعالى . ثم يُسأل كيف كان إن علم أنه كان كذلك في الأزل، فيلزمه الاسم كذلك، أو علم أنه لم يكن، فيلحقه اسم الجهل، وهو بقولهم لازم؛ لأن تأويل العاليم عندهم نفى الجهل، فإذا لم يكن عالما فى القديم فهو إذا عند ذلك كان جاهلا، ولا قوة إلا بالله شيء توحيدهم . فى العلم ؟ إذ لم يكن حتى كان إن حدث، فيجب ذلك في كل ما يقال : كيف حدث به ولم يكن له قدرة ؟ أو بغيره، فيبطل به
It is asked of one who makes these names created: then you do not confirm that Allah had knowledge in pre-eternity, for how was His affair before creation? Did He know His essence or what He does or not? Likewise, did He know His essence as something or did He not know it? If He did not know it, then He is ignorant until He produces knowledge for Himself and becomes knowing by it; and if He knew it, He is knowing; and if He knew it, then is He knowing by knowledge of His essence or not? For if His essence is knowing, then the affirmation of this name in pre-eternity is necessary, and in the otherness of the name is corruption of tawhid. And the principle according to the deniers of attributes is that He did not have this name, and He did not have an attribute that is knowledge by which He knows His essence in pre-eternity, which is necessary according to what Jahm said, who denies the names and attributes and makes them created, so that He is not knowing nor powerful, then becomes knowing. Exalted is Allah above that and high. Then it is asked: how is it that if He knew that He was thus in pre-eternity, then the name likewise applies to Him; or if He knew that He was not, then the name of ignorance applies to Him, and this is a necessary consequence of their statement. For the interpretation of 'the All-Knowing' according to them is the negation of ignorance. So if He was not knowing in pre-eternity, then He was at that time ignorant. And there is no power except by Allah. Something of their tawhid [is invalid]? Concerning knowledge? For if it was not until it occurred, then that is necessary in everything that is said: how did it occur when He had no power? Or by another? Thus it is invalidated.
Source pages p. 665

Commentary
This passage is a refutation (رد) of those who claim that Allah's names are created (حادثة) and who deny eternal attributes, specifically the Jahmiyya (followers of Jahm ibn Safwan). Maturidi presents a logical argument: if the names are created, then consider Allah's knowledge before creation. The questioner must answer whether Allah knew His essence and His actions before creation. If He did not know them, then He was ignorant (جاهل) until He created knowledge for Himself, which is impossible for Allah. If He knew them, then He is knowing (عالم) in pre-eternity, which necessitates that the name 'All-Knowing' (العليم) applies to Him pre-eternally. Denying that the name applies pre-eternally leads to corruption of tawhid (فساد التوحيد). Maturidi then explains the position of the deniers of attributes (منكرى الصفات): they say Allah did not have this name nor an attribute of knowledge in pre-eternity. This implication, according to Jahm, leads to Allah being not knowing and not powerful and then becoming knowing, which is blasphemous. Maturidi summarizes that according to their interpretation, 'All-Knowing' means negation of ignorance. So if Allah was not knowing in pre-eternity, He was ignorant. This is a necessary consequence of their view. He then points out that if knowledge (or any attribute) occurs after not existing, then for everything that occurs, one must ask: how did it occur when He had no power? Or did it occur by another? This invalidates their position.

منكرى الصفات
جهم بن صفوان
