Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That Allah's names being created does not affect His attributes; they can be added later without contradiction.
Correction: Maturidi shows that if names are created, then before that, Allah lacked the corresponding attribute (e.g., knowledge), implying ignorance, which is impossible for Allah.

Checkpoint
What does Maturidi argue is the consequence of denying that Allah had the name 'All-Knowing' in pre-eternity?
A) Allah is still knowing by essence
B) Allah must have been ignorant in pre-eternity
C) The name is not important
D) Allah has no names

Key Takeaway
Allah's names, including Al-'Alim, are eternal because denying their pre-eternity leads to the absurdity that Allah was once ignorant.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever live as if Allah's knowledge of your actions is limited—that He only knows what you tell Him or what you show outwardly? If you truly believed that His knowledge of your every thought, intention, and deed has always existed in pre-eternity, would your private life look different right now? What would you change today?
?
The passage shows that denying Allah's eternal knowledge leads to the absurdity that He was once ignorant. When you sin, do you ever act as if Allah was unaware of that sin before it happened—as if it caught Him by surprise? How does knowing that His knowledge is not created but eternal press you to seek forgiveness with true urgency, knowing He has always known?
?
Maturidi argues that if attributes were created, Allah would have to acquire knowledge after being ignorant. Do you believe that your own knowledge about Allah grows while His remains perfect and unchanged? How does this truth demand that you submit your entire life—past, present, and future—to His timeless knowledge, trusting that He knows what is best for you even before you ask?

The Principle of Divine Names and the Dilemma of Pre-Eternal Knowledge
Maturidi states the principle of names and poses the knowledge dilemma.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that divine names must correspond to real, unchangeable meanings, and that denying God's eternal knowledge leads to a contradiction: either God was ignorant or the name 'Knower' must be eternal.

Core Idea
Names without real meaning are arbitrary; God's knowledge must be eternal.

Maturidi opens by establishing a foundational principle: the names of God are not arbitrary labels but are rooted in verified meanings. If they were not, they would be interchangeable and subject to change, which undermines tawhid. He then immediately applies this to the claim that God's names are created by posing a crucial dilemma about God's knowledge before creation. This sets the stage for refuting those who deny the eternity of divine attributes.

Guided Path
1
Read the opening principle
Read the first sentence of the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice how Maturidi states that if names were not based on true meanings, they could be changed and anything could be called God.
This is a logical groundwork: names must reflect reality.
2
Identify the dilemma
Maturidi then asks: was God knowing His essence before creation or not? Underline the two options and their consequences.
The dilemma forces the opponent to choose between ignorance and eternal knowledge.
3
Trace the conclusion
Follow how Maturidi concludes that if God was knowing, then the name 'Knower' is eternal; if not, He was ignorant. This refutes the createdness of the name.
The conclusion is that the name must be eternal if it is true.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
في التحقيق غيره لاحتمل التبديل، ولصارت التسمية على غير تحقيق المعنى والمفهوم، ولجازت تسميته بكل ما يسمى غيره إذا لم يرد تحقيق المفهوم من [؟]. ما يُسأل من يجعل هذه الأسماء حادثة، ثم لا تحقق الله علما في الأزل إذ كيف كان أمره قبل الخلق، أكان يعلم ذاته أو ما يفعل أو لا؟ وكذلك أكان يعلم ذاته شيئا أو لا يعلمها؟ فإن كان لا يعلمها، فهو إذا جاهل حتى أحدث العلم له فصار به عالما، وإن كان يعلمها عالما، وإن كان يعلمها، فإذا بعلم ذاته عالما أو لا؟ فإن ذاته عالما فلزم القول بهذا الاسم في الأزل، وفي غيرية الاسم فساد [؟] كان التوحيد يعلم. والأصل على قول منكري الصفات إذ لم يكن له هذا الاسم، ولم يكن له صفة هي علم يعلم ذاته في الأزل يجب ما قاله جهم ينفي الأسماء والصفات وحدثها فيكون غير عالم ولا قادر ثم عليم، جل الله عن ذلك وتعالى. ثم يُسأل كيف كان إن علم أنه كان كذلك في الأزل، فيلزمه الاسم كذلك، أو علم أنه لم يكن، فيلحقه اسم الجهل، وهو بقولهم لازم؛ لأن تأويل العالم عندهم نفي الجهل، فإذا لم يكن عالما في القديم فهو إذا عند ذلك كان جاهلا، ولا قوة إلا بالله. شيء توحيدهم. في العلم؟ إذ لم يكن حتى كان إن حدث، فيجب ذلك في كل ما يقال: كيف حدث به ولم يكن له قدرة؟ أو بغيره، فيبطل به. ثم يقال له في الفصل الذي ذكرت: إنه كان يعلم ذاته قبل الخلق يكن له علم في الحقيقة، كيف كان يعلم ذاته؟ فإن كان ذاته عالما يعلم بطل قوله يحدث الاسم، وإن قال: غير عالم، ولا قادر عليه، دخل عليه جميع ما ذكرت، مع إحالة الوصف له بالعلم به في الأزل، مع فساد ما بينا في الحدث، وإن قال من بعد: بغيره، رآه ممن يعترض فيه العوارض، به تكون العالم، وفي ذلك موافقة الدهرية في الطينة، وأصحاب الهيولى والثنوية في كون العالم باعتراض العوارض في الأصل، ولا قوة إلا بالله. وهذه المسألة هي مسألة الصفات في التحقيق، وقد بينا ذلك.
In reality, other than it would have admitted alteration, and naming would not be on the basis of verifying meaning and concept, and it would be permissible to name Him with every name by which another is called if the verification of the concept from [؟] is not intended. What is asked of the one who makes these names created, and then does not verify that God has knowledge in eternity? For how was His state before creation? Was He knowing His essence or what He does or not? And likewise, was He knowing His essence in any way or not knowing it? If He was not knowing it, then He is ignorant until He creates knowledge for Himself and becomes knowing by it. And if He was knowing it, [then He is] knowing. And if He was knowing it, then is He knowing by virtue of His essence? Or not? For if He is knowing by His essence, then the utterance of this name in eternity is necessary, and in the otherness of the name is corruption of [؟] was tawhid. And the foundation, according to the deniers of attributes, is that He did not have this name, and He did not have an attribute that is knowledge by which He knows His essence in eternity; that is what Jahm said, denying the names and attributes and making them created, so that He is not knowing nor powerful, then [He becomes] knowing—exalted is Allah above that and highly exalted. Then he is asked: how is it? If He knew that He was so in eternity, then the name follows likewise; or He knew that He was not, then the name of ignorance attaches to Him, and that is necessary according to their statement because the interpretation of 'the Knower' according to them is the negation of ignorance. So if He was not knowing in pre-eternity, then at that time He was ignorant, and there is no power except with Allah. Something of their tawhid. Regarding knowledge? Since it was not until it came to be by origination, that is necessary in everything that is said: How did it occur while He had no power? Or by another? That would invalidate it. Then it is said to him concerning the section I mentioned: He was knowing His essence before creation? He has no real knowledge; how was He knowing His essence? For if He is knowing by His essence, that refutes his statement that the name is originated. And if he says: not knowing, and not having power over it, then all that I mentioned applies to him, along with the impossibility of describing Him with knowledge in eternity, along with the corruption of what we explained about origination. And if he says afterwards: by another, he would be seen as one who is subject to accidents, by which he becomes knowing. And in that is agreement with the Dahriyya in the primordial matter, and the adherents of hyle and the dualists in the world being subject to accidents in the origin. And there is no power except with Allah. And this issue is the issue of attributes in reality, and we have clarified that.
Source pages p. 665

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the view that God's names and attributes are created, specifically targeting Jahm ibn Safwan. Maturidi begins by stating that if names were not based on verified meanings, they would be interchangeable and meaningless. He then poses a dilemma regarding God's knowledge before creation: either God knew His essence or He did not. If He did not, He would be ignorant until He created knowledge, implying change and imperfection. If He knew, then the name 'Knower' must be eternal. The deniers of attributes (like Jahm) claim God had no attribute of knowledge in eternity, but this leads to the absurd conclusion that God was ignorant. Maturidi further questions: if God knew Himself in eternity, the name is eternal; if not, He was ignorant. The term 'Knower' means negation of ignorance, so pre-eternal absence of knowledge implies ignorance. The argument continues by examining how God had knowledge: if through His essence, the name is eternal; if through another, that would mean dependency on accidents, aligning with materialist and dualist views. Maturidi concludes that this entire discussion is essentially about the attributes (al-sifat).

Key Takeaway
Divine names are not arbitrary; the name 'Knower' must be eternal because God's knowledge cannot be created after nonexistence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

What is one specific situation today where you will consciously remind yourself that He knows perfectly?

If God's knowledge is eternal and unchanging, then every moment of your life—past, present, and future—is known to Him with absolute certainty. How does that truth confront your anxiety about the future or your regret over the past? What is one worry or regret you will consciously surrender to His all-encompassing knowledge today?

Refuting the Createdness of Attributes: The Consequences of Denying Eternal Knowledge
Maturidi refutes Jahm and shows the consequences of denying eternal attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi refutes Jahm ibn Safwan's denial of eternal attributes, showing that it leads to absurdities such as God being ignorant or dependent on accidents.

Core Idea
Denying eternal attributes makes God either ignorant or dependent on creation.

Maturidi now directly confronts the position of Jahm ibn Safwan and those who deny that God has eternal attributes. He shows that their claim—that God did not have the attribute of knowledge in eternity—forces them into a contradiction: either God was ignorant, or knowledge came from an external source, which would make God subject to accidents like material beings. This connects to the broader issue of the divine attributes (al-sifat) and refutes the view that attributes are created.

Guided Path
1
Identify the target: Jahm
Read the lines that mention Jahm by name. Understand that he denied names and attributes and claimed they are created.
Jahm ibn Safwan was a prominent early theologian who held that God's attributes are not eternal.
2
Follow the second dilemma
Maturidi asks: if God knew He was knower in eternity, then the name is eternal; if He knew He was not, then ignorance. This drives home the absurdity.
The term 'Knower' means negation of ignorance, so absence of knowledge implies ignorance.
3
Examine the third option: knowledge from another
If the opponent says knowledge came from something else, that would make God subject to accidents, aligning with materialist and dualist views.
Maturidi equates this with the Dahriyya, hyle, and dualists, which are clearly false.

Source Text

في التحقيق غيره لاحتمل التبديل، ولصارت التسمية على غير تحقيق المعنى والمفهوم، ولجازت تسميته بكل ما يسمى غيره إذا لم يرد تحقيق المفهوم من [؟]. ما يُسأل من يجعل هذه الأسماء حادثة، ثم لا تحقق الله علما في الأزل إذ كيف كان أمره قبل الخلق، أكان يعلم ذاته أو ما يفعل أو لا؟ وكذلك أكان يعلم ذاته شيئا أو لا يعلمها؟ فإن كان لا يعلمها، فهو إذا جاهل حتى أحدث العلم له فصار به عالما، وإن كان يعلمها عالما، وإن كان يعلمها، فإذا بعلم ذاته عالما أو لا؟ فإن ذاته عالما فلزم القول بهذا الاسم في الأزل، وفي غيرية الاسم فساد [؟] كان التوحيد يعلم. والأصل على قول منكري الصفات إذ لم يكن له هذا الاسم، ولم يكن له صفة هي علم يعلم ذاته في الأزل يجب ما قاله جهم ينفي الأسماء والصفات وحدثها فيكون غير عالم ولا قادر ثم عليم، جل الله عن ذلك وتعالى. ثم يُسأل كيف كان إن علم أنه كان كذلك في الأزل، فيلزمه الاسم كذلك، أو علم أنه لم يكن، فيلحقه اسم الجهل، وهو بقولهم لازم؛ لأن تأويل العالم عندهم نفي الجهل، فإذا لم يكن عالما في القديم فهو إذا عند ذلك كان جاهلا، ولا قوة إلا بالله. شيء توحيدهم. في العلم؟ إذ لم يكن حتى كان إن حدث، فيجب ذلك في كل ما يقال: كيف حدث به ولم يكن له قدرة؟ أو بغيره، فيبطل به. ثم يقال له في الفصل الذي ذكرت: إنه كان يعلم ذاته قبل الخلق يكن له علم في الحقيقة، كيف كان يعلم ذاته؟ فإن كان ذاته عالما يعلم بطل قوله يحدث الاسم، وإن قال: غير عالم، ولا قادر عليه، دخل عليه جميع ما ذكرت، مع إحالة الوصف له بالعلم به في الأزل، مع فساد ما بينا في الحدث، وإن قال من بعد: بغيره، رآه ممن يعترض فيه العوارض، به تكون العالم، وفي ذلك موافقة الدهرية في الطينة، وأصحاب الهيولى والثنوية في كون العالم باعتراض العوارض في الأصل، ولا قوة إلا بالله. وهذه المسألة هي مسألة الصفات في التحقيق، وقد بينا ذلك.
In reality, other than it would have admitted alteration, and naming would not be on the basis of verifying meaning and concept, and it would be permissible to name Him with every name by which another is called if the verification of the concept from [؟] is not intended. What is asked of the one who makes these names created, and then does not verify that God has knowledge in eternity? For how was His state before creation? Was He knowing His essence or what He does or not? And likewise, was He knowing His essence in any way or not knowing it? If He was not knowing it, then He is ignorant until He creates knowledge for Himself and becomes knowing by it. And if He was knowing it, [then He is] knowing. And if He was knowing it, then is He knowing by virtue of His essence? Or not? For if He is knowing by His essence, then the utterance of this name in eternity is necessary, and in the otherness of the name is corruption of [؟] was tawhid. And the foundation, according to the deniers of attributes, is that He did not have this name, and He did not have an attribute that is knowledge by which He knows His essence in eternity; that is what Jahm said, denying the names and attributes and making them created, so that He is not knowing nor powerful, then [He becomes] knowing—exalted is Allah above that and highly exalted. Then he is asked: how is it? If He knew that He was so in eternity, then the name follows likewise; or He knew that He was not, then the name of ignorance attaches to Him, and that is necessary according to their statement because the interpretation of 'the Knower' according to them is the negation of ignorance. So if He was not knowing in pre-eternity, then at that time He was ignorant, and there is no power except with Allah. Something of their tawhid. Regarding knowledge? Since it was not until it came to be by origination, that is necessary in everything that is said: How did it occur while He had no power? Or by another? That would invalidate it. Then it is said to him concerning the section I mentioned: He was knowing His essence before creation? He has no real knowledge; how was He knowing His essence? For if He is knowing by His essence, that refutes his statement that the name is originated. And if he says: not knowing, and not having power over it, then all that I mentioned applies to him, along with the impossibility of describing Him with knowledge in eternity, along with the corruption of what we explained about origination. And if he says afterwards: by another, he would be seen as one who is subject to accidents, by which he becomes knowing. And in that is agreement with the Dahriyya in the primordial matter, and the adherents of hyle and the dualists in the world being subject to accidents in the origin. And there is no power except with Allah. And this issue is the issue of attributes in reality, and we have clarified that.
Source pages p. 665

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the view that God's names and attributes are created, specifically targeting Jahm ibn Safwan. Maturidi begins by stating that if names were not based on verified meanings, they would be interchangeable and meaningless. He then poses a dilemma regarding God's knowledge before creation: either God knew His essence or He did not. If He did not, He would be ignorant until He created knowledge, implying change and imperfection. If He knew, then the name 'Knower' must be eternal. The deniers of attributes (like Jahm) claim God had no attribute of knowledge in eternity, but this leads to the absurd conclusion that God was ignorant. Maturidi further questions: if God knew Himself in eternity, the name is eternal; if not, He was ignorant. The term 'Knower' means negation of ignorance, so pre-eternal absence of knowledge implies ignorance. The argument continues by examining how God had knowledge: if through His essence, the name is eternal; if through another, that would mean dependency on accidents, aligning with materialist and dualist views. Maturidi concludes that this entire discussion is essentially about the attributes (al-sifat).

الصفات
جاهل
الاسم
الأزل
الدهرية
الهيولى
الثنوية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That Maturidi is merely repeating a logical game without real theological weight.
Correction: Maturidi demonstrates that denying eternal attributes leads to theological contradictions: either God was ignorant or dependent on creation, which are both impossible for the divine.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, what does the term 'Knower' mean for those who deny attributes?
A) Possession of knowledge
B) Negation of ignorance
C) Acquisition of knowledge
D) Essence of God

Key Takeaway
Denying that God has eternal attributes forces one into absurdities, affirming the necessity of attributes like knowledge.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You say you believe God knows everything, but if His knowledge were not eternal, could you truly rely on His promises? How does this passage force you to reexamine your trust in God's unchanging nature?
?
Are there areas of your life where you act as if God is 'learning' about your situation? What would change if you truly believed His knowledge was eternal and complete?
?
If you deny any of God's eternal attributes—like power or knowledge—you risk making Him dependent on creation. Are you willing to accept that implication? What will you do today to affirm His perfection?

The Disagreement on the Throne (Arsh)
Maturidi presents the disagreement among Muslims about describing God as being on the Throne.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the early Muslim disagreement about whether Allah is described as being on the Throne, and the scriptural proofs cited by those who affirm a literal interpretation.

Core Idea
The Throne (Arsh) debate centers on whether Allah is physically on the Throne, as some Muslims argued using Qur'anic verses.

In this passage, Imam Maturidi reports a key theological disagreement among early Muslims: some held that Allah is literally established on the Throne, interpreting 'Arsh' as a physical couch carried by angels. They supported their view with several Qur'anic verses. Let's read the passage and understand their position.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the literal translation. Notice how Maturidi frames the disagreement.
Maturidi is reporting, not affirming, this view.
2
Identify the two positions
The passage mentions that Muslims disagreed about describing Allah with 'place' (al-makan). One group claimed He is described as being established on the Throne.
The other group's view is not detailed here.
3
Examine the scriptural proofs
List the Qur'anic verses cited: 69:17, 39:75, 40:7, and 20:5. Notice how each verse is used to support the literal interpretation.
The main proof is 20:5: 'The Most Merciful established Himself upon the Throne.'
4
Understand the conclusion
The group concludes that the Throne is a physical object carried by angels and that Allah is established upon it. Maturidi presents this without refutation here.
This sets up the debate for later discussion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة بيان العرش. قال أبو منصور رضي الله عنه: ثم اختلف أهل الإسلام في القول بالمكان فمنهم من زعم أنه يوصف بأنه على العرش مستو، والعرش عندهم السرير المحمول بالملائكة المحفوف بهم: وَيَحْمِلُ عَرْشَ رَبِّكَ فَوقَهُم يَوْمَئِذٍ ثَمَانِيَة، وقوله وَتَرَى المَلائِكَةَ حَافِّينَ مِنْ حَوْلِ العَرْشِ، وقوله: الَّذِينَ يَحْمِلُونَ العَرْش وَمَنْ حَوْلَهُ. واحتجوا للقول به بقوله: الرَّحْمَنُ عَلَى العَرْشِ اسْتَوَى.
The issue of clarifying the Throne. Abu Mansur (may Allah be pleased with him) said: Then the people of Islam disagreed concerning the statement about place. Among them are those who claimed that He is described as being established on the Throne, and the Throne according to them is the couch carried by the angels surrounding them: 'And eight will bear the Throne of your Lord above them that Day' (69:17), and His statement: 'And you see the angels surrounding the Throne' (39:75), and His statement: 'Those who bear the Throne and those around it' (40:7). And they argued for this statement with His statement: 'The Most Merciful established Himself upon the Throne' (20:5).
Source pages p. 666

Commentary
This passage begins a new topic: the clarification of the Throne (al-arsh). Maturidi reports that Muslims disagreed about describing Allah with place (al-makan). Some held that Allah is described as being established (mustawin) on the Throne, interpreting 'al-arsh' as a physical couch carried by angels. They support their view with Quranic verses describing angels carrying the Throne (69:17), angels surrounding it (39:75), and those who bear the Throne and those around it (40:7). Their main proof is the verse 'The Most Merciful established Himself upon the Throne' (20:5). Maturidi presents their position without yet giving a refutation, setting up the debate.

Key Takeaway
Muslims disagreed about whether Allah is on the Throne; some argued from the Qur'an that He is established on it, interpreting 'Arsh' as a physical throne carried by angels.

The Trilemma on God's Knowledge and the Creation of Names
Maturidi refutes a position on God's knowledge and the creation of divine names.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's logical refutation of the claim that divine names are created through a trilemma about God's knowledge.

Core Idea
God's eternal knowledge disproves the createdness of His names.

Imam Maturidi responds to those who argue that the names of God are created. He presents a logical trilemma: either God knew His essence before creation through His essence, or He did not know it, or He knew it through something else. Each option leads to a contradiction or an unacceptable consequence, thereby defending the eternity of God's names.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
First, read the Arabic passage and its literal translation to grasp the overall argument. Note the three options presented and the flow of reasoning.
The passage is a single continuous argument against the createdness of divine names.
2
Identify the three possibilities
Maturidi examines three ways God could have known His essence before creation: through His essence (option 1), not knowing (option 2), or through something else (option 3). Identify each and see how they are discussed.
These three options form a trilemma: each leads to a rebuttal.
3
Analyze the consequences of each option
For option 1, if God's essence is knowing, then the claim that names are created is false. For option 2, if God is not knowing, absurdities follow. For option 3, if through something else, it leads to agreement with materialist and dualist positions. Trace these consequences.
Option 3 leads to an especially strong refutation by associating the opponent with disbelievers.
4
Connect to the broader theological context
Reflect on how this argument upholds the doctrine of divine attributes (sifat) and the eternity of God's names, central to Maturidi theology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم يقال له فى الفصل الذي ذكرت : إنه كان يعلم ذاته قبل الخلق يكن له علم في الحقيقة ، كيف كان يعلم ذاته ؟ فإن كان ذاته عالما يعلم بطل قوله يحدث الاسم ، وإن قال : غير عالم ، ولا قادر عليه ، دخل عليه جميع ما ذكرت ، مع إحالة الوصف له بالعلم به في الأزل ، مع فساد ما بينا في الحدث ، وإن قال من بعد : بغيره ، رآه ممن يعترض فيه العوارض ، به تكون العالم ، وفى ذلك موافقة الدهرية في الطينة ، وأصحاب الهيولى والثنوية في كون العالم باعتراض العوارض في الأصل ، ولا قوة إلا بالله .
Then it is said to him in the chapter you mentioned: That He knew His essence before creation; He had knowledge in reality. How did He know His essence? For if His essence is knowing, He knows – his statement that the name is created is invalidated. And if he says: not knowing and not able over it, all that I mentioned applies to him, along with the impossibility of describing Him with knowledge of it in pre-eternity, along with the corruption of what we explained about [the] originated. And if he says later: by other than it, he sees him as one who objects that accidents occur in it, by which the world comes to be. And in that is agreement with the Dahriyya in [the] clay/nature, and the proponents of hyle and the dualists in [the] world's existence by the occurrence of accidents in the origin. And there is no power except with God.
Source pages p. 666

Commentary
This passage is a refutation (dilemma) of a certain position regarding God's knowledge and the creation of divine names. It addresses someone who holds that the name of God is created. The argument proceeds by examining how God could have known His own essence before creation. The refutation presents three possible answers: if God's essence itself is knowing and learns (i.e., knowledge is essential), then the claim that the name is created is false; if God is not knowing and not able (i.e., denies knowledge), then all the previously mentioned consequences apply, including the impossibility of describing Him as knowing in eternity; if one says that God knows through something other than His essence, then that other thing would be subject to accidents, leading to agreement with materialist and dualist philosophies. The conclusion is that these positions are impossible.

Key Terms
ذاته
العلم
الاسم
الحدث
الدهرية
الهيولى
الثنوية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that denying God's knowledge leads to atheism, but Maturidi's point is that it leads to logical absurdity and agreement with materialist philosophies.
Correction: Maturidi shows that denying God's knowledge (or claiming it through something else) results in contradictions or aligning with rejected views, not merely disbelief.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the consequence of claiming that God knows His essence through something other than His essence?
A) It invalidates the creation of names.
B) It leads to agreement with the Dahriyya and dualists.
C) It proves God's power.
D) It is impossible to describe God.

Key Takeaway
Maturidi's trilemma defends the eternity of God's names by showing that any alternative leads to either logical contradiction or agreement with discredited philosophies.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite the name 'Allah', do you recognize that this name is not a human invention but flows from God's eternal knowledge? How would you feel if you treated it as a mere word?
?
If you were asked to defend the eternity of God's names, could you articulate this trilemma? What does your comfort or discomfort with logical arguments about God reveal about the strength of your faith?
?
This passage rejects views that align with materialism and dualism. Have you ever unconsciously adopted ideas that reduce God's transcendence to fit human limitations? What would it take to purify your creed from such influences?

The View that Allah is on the Throne
Maturidi reports the first view on place.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the first Islamic view that Allah is physically established on the Throne and the scriptural proofs they cite.

Core Idea
Some Muslims believe Allah is literally on the Throne above.

Maturidi begins by reporting the first group among Ahl al-Islam who affirm a literal place for Allah: the Throne. They interpret verses about the Throne and establishment (istiwa) literally and argue that raising hands in supplication indicates a direction. This lesson examines their evidence and reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation to see how Maturidi describes this group's beliefs and their proofs.
Notice they use multiple verses.
2
Identify the arguments
List the verses they cite: the Throne verses, the istiwa verse, and the practice of raising hands. Understand why they think these prove a literal place.
3
Consider the implications
Think about why this view might be problematic. What does it imply about Allah's relation to creation?
This connects to later lessons.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة بيان العرش قال أبو منصور رضى الله عنه : ثم اختلف أهل الإسلام في القول بالمكان فمنهم من زعم أنه يوصف بأنه على العرش مستو ، والعرش عندهم السرير المحمول بالملائكة المحفوف بهم : وَيَحْمِلُ عَرْشَ رَبِّكَ فَوقَهُم يَوْمَئِذٍ ثَمَانِيَة ، وقوله وَتَرَى المَلائِكَةُ حَافِّينَ مِنْ حَوْلِ العَرْشِ ، وقوله : الَّذِينَ يَحْمِلُونَ العَرْش وَمَنْ حَوْلَهُ . واحتجوا للقول به بقوله : الرَّحْمَنُ عَلَى العَرْشِ اسْتَوَى ، ويرفع الناس إلى السماء بالدعوات أيديهم وما يأملون من الخيرات ، ويقولون : هو صار إليه بعد أن لم يكن لقوله : ثُمَّ اسْتَوَى عَلَى العَرْشِ . ومنهم من يقول هو بكل مكان بقوله : مَا يَكُونُ مِنْ نَجْوَى ثَلَاثَةٍ إِلَّا هُوَ وقوله : وَنَحْنُ أَقْرَبُ إِلَيْهِ مِنْ حَبْل الْوَرِيدِ ، وقوله : وَنَحْنُ أَقْرَبُ إِلَيْهِ مِنْكُمْ وَلَكِنْ لَا تُبْصِرُونَ ، وقوله : الَّذِي فِي السَّمَاءِ وهو وفي الأرض وظنوا أن القول بأنه في مكان دون مكان يوجب الحد ، وكل ذي جاء مقصر عما هو أعظم منه ، وذلك عيب وآفة ، وفى ذلك إيجاب الحاجة ما فيه إيجاب الحد ؛ إذ لا يحتمل أن يكون أعظم من المكان لما سخف فى المتعارف أن يختار أحد مكانا لا يسعه ، فيصير حد المكان حده إلى المكان هو مع جل ربنا عن ذلك وتعالى . ومنهم من قال بنفي الوصف بالمكان، وكذلك بالأمكنة كلها إلا على مجاز اللغة بمعنى الحافظ لها والقائم بها . قال الشيخ أبو منصور رحمه الله : وجملة ذلك أن إضافة كلية الأشياء إليه ، وإضافته عز وجل إليها يخرج مخرج الوصف له بالعلو والرفعة ومخرج التعظيم له والجلال كقوله : لَهُ مُلْكُ السَّمَاوَاتِ وَالأَرْضِ ، رَبُّ السَّمَاوَاتِ وَالأَرْضِ إلى الخلق ، رب العالمين ، وفوق كل شيء ونحوه . وإضافة الخاص إليه يخرج
Issue: Explanation of the Throne. Abu Mansur said: Then the people of Islam disagreed regarding the statement about place. Some claim that He is described as being established on the Throne, and the Throne according to them is the bed carried by the angels surrounded by them: 'And on that day eight will bear the Throne of your Lord above them' and His saying: 'And you see the angels surrounding the Throne' and His saying: 'Those who bear the Throne and those around it.' And they argued for this by His saying: 'The Most Merciful is established on the Throne.' And people raise their hands to the sky in supplication and what they hope of good things, and they say: He ascended to it after not having been, because of His saying: 'Then He established Himself on the Throne.' And among them are those who say He is in every place by His saying: 'There is no secret conversation of three except that He is the fourth' and His saying: 'And We are nearer to him than the jugular vein' and His saying: 'And We are nearer to him than you, but you do not see' and His saying: 'He who is in the heaven and He in the earth' – and they thought that saying He is in one place without another necessitates limitation, and everything that comes is deficient compared to what is greater, and that is a defect and affliction; and in that is necessitating need, which necessitates limitation; for it is not possible that He be greater than place because of the absurdity in common knowledge that one chooses a place that does not contain Him, so the limit of place becomes His limit? – with the majesty of our Lord and His highness above that. And among them are those who deny the description with place, and likewise with all places, except metaphorically in language meaning the Preserver and Sustainer of them. Sheikh Abu Mansur said: The summary of that is that the general attribution of all things to Him, and His attribution to them, comes in the form of describing Him with highness and elevation and in the form of magnifying Him and majesty, like His saying: 'To Him belongs the dominion of the heavens and the earth' and 'Lord of the heavens and the earth' and 'to the creation' and 'Lord of the worlds' and 'above all things' and the like. And the specific attribution to Him is...
Source pages p. 666

Commentary
This passage is a classification and resolution of differing views on whether Allah inherits a place. Maturidi first reports two main views among Ahl al-Islam: first, the Anthropomorphist view that He is literally on the Throne above, citing verses that speak of the Throne and establishment; second, the multi-religious movement, citing verses about closeness and omnipresence. Then he reports a third view that denies spatial description except as a linguistic metaphor meaning preservation. Finally, Maturidi gives his own synthesis: all such attributions are only expressions of His highness and majesty, not actual spatial relations. He illustrates with verses that attribute dominion and lordship.

Key Terms
العرش
الاستواء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the main scriptural proof cited by those who say Allah is on the Throne?
A) 'There is no secret conversation of three...'
B) 'The Most Merciful is established on the Throne.'
C) 'And We are nearer to him than the jugular vein.'
D) 'To Him belongs the dominion of the heavens and the earth.'

Key Takeaway
The first group believes Allah is literally on the Throne, citing verses on istiwa and the angels carrying the Throne.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter a Muslim who believes Allah is literally on the Throne does your heart react with humility or with rejection? What does that reveal about your own attachment to your theological position?
?
This passage shows that early Muslims disagreed on a fundamental issue. Are you willing to admit that your own understanding might be one among many, or do you cling to certainty where the scholars differed?
?
The first group cited verses to prove their view. Are you equally diligent in grounding your beliefs in revelation, or do you rely on inherited opinions without examining the evidence?

The View that Allah is Everywhere
Maturidi reports the second view on place.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the second view that Allah is everywhere, their scriptural proofs, and their critique of the first view.

Core Idea
Others argue that Allah is present everywhere, citing closeness verses.

The second group among Ahl al-Islam holds that Allah is in every place, not confined to the Throne. They cite verses about closeness and omnipresence, and they argue that saying He is in one place limits Him. This lesson explores their evidence and reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the description of this group's belief and the verses they use.
2
Understand their critique
They argue that specifying a place imposes limitation (hadd). See how they reason that such limitation is a defect.
3
Reflect on the issue
Consider the tension between the two views: one says above, the other says everywhere. Which seems more consistent with divine transcendence?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة بيان العرش قال أبو منصور رضى الله عنه : ثم اختلف أهل الإسلام في القول بالمكان فمنهم من زعم أنه يوصف بأنه على العرش مستو ، والعرش عندهم السرير المحمول بالملائكة المحفوف بهم : وَيَحْمِلُ عَرْشَ رَبِّكَ فَوقَهُم يَوْمَئِذٍ ثَمَانِيَة ، وقوله وَتَرَى المَلائِكَةُ حَافِّينَ مِنْ حَوْلِ العَرْشِ ، وقوله : الَّذِينَ يَحْمِلُونَ العَرْش وَمَنْ حَوْلَهُ . واحتجوا للقول به بقوله : الرَّحْمَنُ عَلَى العَرْشِ اسْتَوَى ، ويرفع الناس إلى السماء بالدعوات أيديهم وما يأملون من الخيرات ، ويقولون : هو صار إليه بعد أن لم يكن لقوله : ثُمَّ اسْتَوَى عَلَى العَرْشِ . ومنهم من يقول هو بكل مكان بقوله : مَا يَكُونُ مِنْ نَجْوَى ثَلَاثَةٍ إِلَّا هُوَ وقوله : وَنَحْنُ أَقْرَبُ إِلَيْهِ مِنْ حَبْل الْوَرِيدِ ، وقوله : وَنَحْنُ أَقْرَبُ إِلَيْهِ مِنْكُمْ وَلَكِنْ لَا تُبْصِرُونَ ، وقوله : الَّذِي فِي السَّمَاءِ وهو وفي الأرض وظنوا أن القول بأنه في مكان دون مكان يوجب الحد ، وكل ذي جاء مقصر عما هو أعظم منه ، وذلك عيب وآفة ، وفى ذلك إيجاب الحاجة ما فيه إيجاب الحد ؛ إذ لا يحتمل أن يكون أعظم من المكان لما سخف فى المتعارف أن يختار أحد مكانا لا يسعه ، فيصير حد المكان حده إلى المكان هو مع جل ربنا عن ذلك وتعالى . ومنهم من قال بنفي الوصف بالمكان، وكذلك بالأمكنة كلها إلا على مجاز اللغة بمعنى الحافظ لها والقائم بها . قال الشيخ أبو منصور رحمه الله : وجملة ذلك أن إضافة كلية الأشياء إليه ، وإضافته عز وجل إليها يخرج مخرج الوصف له بالعلو والرفعة ومخرج التعظيم له والجلال كقوله : لَهُ مُلْكُ السَّمَاوَاتِ وَالأَرْضِ ، رَبُّ السَّمَاوَاتِ وَالأَرْضِ إلى الخلق ، رب العالمين ، وفوق كل شيء ونحوه . وإضافة الخاص إليه يخرج
Issue: Explanation of the Throne. Abu Mansur said: Then the people of Islam disagreed regarding the statement about place. Some claim that He is described as being established on the Throne, and the Throne according to them is the bed carried by the angels surrounded by them: 'And on that day eight will bear the Throne of your Lord above them' and His saying: 'And you see the angels surrounding the Throne' and His saying: 'Those who bear the Throne and those around it.' And they argued for this by His saying: 'The Most Merciful is established on the Throne.' And people raise their hands to the sky in supplication and what they hope of good things, and they say: He ascended to it after not having been, because of His saying: 'Then He established Himself on the Throne.' And among them are those who say He is in every place by His saying: 'There is no secret conversation of three except that He is the fourth' and His saying: 'And We are nearer to him than the jugular vein' and His saying: 'And We are nearer to him than you, but you do not see' and His saying: 'He who is in the heaven and He in the earth' – and they thought that saying He is in one place without another necessitates limitation, and everything that comes is deficient compared to what is greater, and that is a defect and affliction; and in that is necessitating need, which necessitates limitation; for it is not possible that He be greater than place because of the absurdity in common knowledge that one chooses a place that does not contain Him, so the limit of place becomes His limit? – with the majesty of our Lord and His highness above that. And among them are those who deny the description with place, and likewise with all places, except metaphorically in language meaning the Preserver and Sustainer of them. Sheikh Abu Mansur said: The summary of that is that the general attribution of all things to Him, and His attribution to them, comes in the form of describing Him with highness and elevation and in the form of magnifying Him and majesty, like His saying: 'To Him belongs the dominion of the heavens and the earth' and 'Lord of the heavens and the earth' and 'to the creation' and 'Lord of the worlds' and 'above all things' and the like. And the specific attribution to Him is...
Source pages p. 666

Commentary
This passage is a classification and resolution of differing views on whether Allah inherits a place. Maturidi first reports two main views among Ahl al-Islam: first, the Anthropomorphist view that He is literally on the Throne above, citing verses that speak of the Throne and establishment; second, the multi-religious movement, citing verses about closeness and omnipresence. Then he reports a third view that denies spatial description except as a linguistic metaphor meaning preservation. Finally, Maturidi gives his own synthesis: all such attributions are only expressions of His highness and majesty, not actual spatial relations. He illustrates with verses that attribute dominion and lordship.

Key Terms
المكان
الحد
النَّجْوَى

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which verse do the proponents of the 'everywhere' view NOT cite according to the passage?
A) 'There is no secret conversation of three...'
B) 'The Most Merciful is established on the Throne.'
C) 'And We are nearer to him than the jugular vein.'
D) 'He who is in the heaven and He in the earth.'

Key Takeaway
The second group insists that Allah cannot be confined to a single place and interprets closeness verses as evidence for His omnipresence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you feel distant from Allah, do you instinctively look up to the sky? This lesson presents a view that He is everywhere. How does this affect your awareness of His presence in your daily life, even in moments of sin or forgetfulness? Will you commit to a daily reminder that He is closer than your own jugular vein?
?
The second group argued that confining Allah to one place imposes a boundary. Reflect: have you unconsciously limited Allah's mercy or power by assuming He cannot reach you in your current situation? What would change if you truly believed He is present everywhere, including in your hardest moments? Make a concrete plan to turn to Him right where you are.
?
The common misunderstanding is that this view means Allah is physically distributed. But the intended meaning is His knowledge and presence. Ask yourself: when you say 'Allah is with me,' do you truly feel His oversight and care, or is it a mere phrase? What would it take for you to live as if He is indeed closer than your own vein?

The Metaphorical View and Maturidi's Resolution
Maturidi reports the third view and gives his conclusion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the third view that denies spatial description except metaphorically, and Maturidi's own conclusion that all attributions indicate highness and majesty.

Core Idea
All language about Allah's place is metaphorical for His majesty.

Having presented two literalist views, Maturidi now reports a third group that rejects spatial descriptions of Allah altogether, interpreting them as linguistic metaphors for His preservation. Then Maturidi gives his own synthesis: all attributions like 'above' or 'dominion' are expressions of His highness and majesty, not literal location.

Guided Path
1
Read the third view
The third group says 'no place' except metaphorically as Preserver. Understand their position.
2
Read Maturidi's summary
Maturidi states that general attributions (like 'Lord of the worlds') are for highness and majesty, not location.
He distinguishes between general and specific attributions.
3
Synthesize the lesson
Consider how Maturidi resolves the conflict by reinterpreting spatial language as figurative.
That is his approach to divine transcendence.

Understanding Quranic Attributions: General vs Specific
Maturidi explains the two types of divine attributions in the Quran.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam al-Maturidi interprets Quranic attributions of all things to Allah as signs of His transcendence and majesty, not physical location.

Core Idea
Quranic attributions always indicate highness and honor, never spatial dwelling.

Imam al-Maturidi, in this passage from Kitab al-Tawhid, addresses a common confusion: when the Quran attributes things to Allah—whether generally (like 'Lord of the worlds') or specifically (like 'house of Allah')—what do these expressions mean? He explains that they are not to be taken as literal possession or location, but as indications of Allah's transcendence and the honor bestowed upon those things. Let's explore his reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without overthinking. Then read the literal translation to grasp the overall meaning.
Pay attention to the examples given.
2
Distinguish general vs specific attributions
Identify the two categories Maturidi mentions: general attribution (إضافة كلية) and specific attribution (إضافة خاصة). Note the different purposes: general for transcendent majesty, specific for honor and distinction.
3
Reflect on the misinterpretation avoided
Consider the common misunderstanding that 'house of Allah' or 'she-camel of Allah' implies a physical relationship. Maturidi clarifies that such phrases convey honor, not containment.
This is key for a sound understanding of divine transcendence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال الشيخ أبو منصور رحمه الله : وجملة ذلك أن إضافة كلية الأشياء إليه ، وإضافته عز وجل إليها يخرج مخرج الوصف له بالعلو والرفعة ومخرج التعظيم له والجلال كقوله : لَهُ مُلْكُ السَّمَاوَاتِ وَالأَرْضِ ، رَبُّ السَّمَاوَاتِ والأَرْضِ إلى الخلق ، رب العالمين ، وفوق كل شيء ونحوه . وإضافة الخاص إليه يخرج مخرج الاختصاص له بالكرامة والمنزلة والتفضيل له على من هو بجوهره نحو قوله : إِنَّ اللَّهَ مَعَ الَّذِينَ اتَّقَوا وقوله : إِنَّ المَسَاجِدَ اللَّهِ ، نَاقَةَ اللهِ ، بيت الله وغير ذلك ، ولا يخرج شيء من ذلك على مثل المفهوم من إضافة الخلق بعضهم إلى بعض ، لا قطع احتمال مثله في الخلق ، إذ قد تخرج أيضا إضافة التخصيص مخرج التفضيل ، والعموم مخرج فضل السلطان والولاية .
Shaykh Abu Mansur (may Allah have mercy on him) said: The summary of that is that the general attribution of all things to Him, and His attribution to them, comes in the form of describing Him with highness and elevation, and in the form of glorification and majesty, such as His saying: 'To Him belongs the kingdom of the heavens and the earth' (Quran 5:120), 'Lord of the heavens and the earth' (Quran 13:16), and to the creation, 'Lord of the worlds' (Quran 1:2), and 'Above everything' (Quran 6:18), and similar. And specific attribution to Him comes in the form of specification to Him of honor, status, and preference over others by His essence, such as His saying: 'Indeed, Allah is with those who fear Him' (Quran 16:128), and His saying: 'Indeed, the mosques belong to Allah' (Quran 72:18), 'the she-camel of Allah' (Quran 91:13), 'the house of Allah' (Quran 106:3), and other than that. And none of that comes in the sense understood from the attribution of some creatures to others, not even cutting off the possibility of the like of that in creatures, since specific attribution also comes in the form of preference, and general attribution in the form of the excellence of authority and governance.
Source pages p. 667

Commentary
This passage is a summary explanation by Imam al-Maturidi of how Quranic attributions should be understood. He states that when all things (e.g., heavens, earth, creation) are attributed to God in a general sense (إضافة كلية), the purpose is to describe Him with transcendence (علو) and glorification (تعظيم). Examples include 'To Him belongs the kingdom of the heavens and the earth' and 'Lord of the worlds.' These do not imply spatial location but majesty. Similarly, specific attributions (إضافة خاصة) like 'the house of Allah' or 'the she-camel of Allah' indicate honor and distinction, not that God physically dwells in a place. The author emphasizes that such attributions are not to be understood in the same way as creatures attributing something to each other (e.g., 'so-and-so's house'), which would imply possession or physical containment. Rather, they convey either honor (for specific) or authority (for general).

Key Terms
إضافة كلية
إضافة خاصة
علو
تعظيم
اختصاص

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The phrase 'house of Allah' means Allah physically resides in that place.
Correction: Maturidi explains that such specific attributions are meant to honor and sanctify, not to indicate spatial containment.

Checkpoint
What is the purpose of specific attributions like 'house of Allah' according to Maturidi?
A) To indicate God's physical location.
B) To show honor and preference.
C) To prove God is composed of parts.
D) To limit God's boundaries.

Key Takeaway
Quranic attributions to Allah are not to be understood literally as possession or location, but as expressions of His transcendence and His honoring of certain things.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you visit a mosque and call it 'the house of Allah,' do you ever subconsciously imagine Allah dwelling there in a physical sense? How does this lesson challenge that, and what changes in your heart when you see the mosque as a place honored by Allah rather than a residence?
?
The verse 'Indeed, Allah is with those who fear Him' is a specific attribution. Does this make you feel that Allah's 'withness' is a special honor that demands your reverence? What would it mean for your daily life if you truly lived as if Allah's presence with you is not casual but a sign of His favor?

The Three Literal Possibilities of Istiwa and Their Refutation
Maturidi enumerates three literal interpretations of istiwa and refutes each.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three possible literal interpretations of Allah's being on the Throne and why Maturidi refutes each as impossible.

Core Idea
Literal readings of istiwa lead to absurdities like limitation, equality, or deficiency.

Maturidi begins by identifying three possible literal meanings of 'being on the Throne' if taken physically: encompassment, equality, or surpassing. Each possibility leads to an absurd consequence incompatible with Allah's perfection. This lesson examines the trilemma.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic text once to get the rhythm, then read the translation. Notice the three possibilities presented.
The passage is dense; take your time.
2
Identify the three possibilities
Find and list the three literal interpretations Maturidi considers. They are: encompassment by the Throne, equality with it, and surpassing/encompassing it.
3
Understand each refutation
For each possibility, note the absurd consequence Maturidi points out: limitation, need, or deficiency. Ask yourself why these are impossible for Allah.
This connects to the core idea.
4
Reflect on the implications
Consider why Maturidi starts with this trilemma. It shows that any literal interpretation fails, forcing a metaphorical understanding.
This paves the way for the positive interpretation later.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال أبو منصور رحمه الله : / ثم القول بالكون على العرش بمعنى كونه بذاته أو في كل الأمكنة - لا يعدو من إحاطة ذلك به ، أو الاستواء به ، أو مجاوزته عنه وإحاطته به ، فإن كان الأول فهو إذا محدود به محاط منقوص عن الخلق إذ هو دونه ، ولو جاز الوصف له بذاته بما يحيط به [من] لجاز بما يحيط به [من] الأوقات فيصير متناهيا بذاته مقصراً عن خلقه ، وإن كان على الوجه الثاني فلو زيد على الخلق لا ينقص أيضا ، وفيه ما في الأول وإن كان على الوجه الثالث فهو الأمر المكروه الدال على الحاجة وعلى التقصير أن ينشئ ما لا يفضل عنه ، مع ما يذم ذا من فعل الملوك أن لا يفضل فيهم من المحامد شيئا . وبعد ، فإن في ذلك تجزئة بما كان بعضه فى ذى أبعاض ، وبعضه يفضل وذلك كله وصف الخلائق ، والله يتعالى عن ذلك . وبعد ، فإنه ليس في الارتفاع إلى ما يعلو من المكان للجلوس أو القيام شرف ولا علو ولا وصف بالعظمة والكبرياء ، كمن يعلو السطوح أو الجبال إنه لا يستحق الرفعة على من دونه عند استواء الجوهر ، فلا يجوز صرف تأويل الآية إليه، مع ماا فيها ذكر العظمة والجلال. إذ ذكر في قوله تعالى : إِنَّ رَبَّكُمُ اللَّهُ الَّذِي خَلَقَ السَّمَاوَاتِ والأرْضِ فدلك على تعظيم العرش ، أي شيء كان من نور أو جوهر لا يبلغه علم الخلق . وقد روى عن نبي الله صلى الله عليه وسلم أنه وصف الشمس أن جبريل يأتيها بكف من ضوء العرش فيلبسها كما يلبس أحدكم قميصه كل يوم تطلع ، وذكر فى القمر كفاً من نور العرش، فإضافة الاستواء إليه / لوجهين : أحدهما على تعظيمه بما ذكره على أثر ذكر سلطانه فى ربوبيته وخلقه ما ذكر والثاني على تخصيصه بالذكر بما هو أعظم الخلق وأجله ، على المعروف من إضافة الأمور العظيمة إلى أعظم الأشياء كما يقال : تم لفلان ملك بلد كذا واستوى
Abu Mansur (may Allah have mercy on him) said: Then the statement about being on the Throne, meaning His being in His essence or in every place, does not go beyond one of three: encompassment by it (the Throne), equality with it, or surpassing it and encompassing it. If it is the first, then He is limited by it, encompassed, diminished relative to creation, since He is beneath it. And if it were permissible to describe Him in His essence as that which is encompassed by [place?], then it would be permissible for Him to be encompassed by [times?], and He would become finite in His essence, falling short of His creation. If it is the second aspect, then if creation were increased, He would not be short either, and in it is what is in the first. If it is the third aspect, then it is the disliked matter which indicates need and deficiency: that He originates what does not exceed Him, along with the blameworthiness of the action of kings that they do not excel in praiseworthy things. Furthermore, in that there is division involving something wherein some of it has parts, and some of it exceeds; all of that is the description of creatures, and Allah is exalted above that. Furthermore, rising to a high place for sitting or standing does not confer honor, loftiness, or description of greatness and majesty, like one who ascends roofs or mountains: he does not deserve elevation over those below him when the essence is equal. So it is not permissible to apply the interpretation of the verse to that, especially since in it there is mention of greatness and majesty. For He mentioned in His statement: 'Indeed, your Lord is Allah who created the heavens and the earth' so that indicates the magnifying of the Throne, whatever it may be of light or essence that the knowledge of creation does not attain. It has been reported from the Prophet of Allah (peace be upon him) that he described the sun: that Gabriel brings to it a handful of light from the Throne and clothes it as one of you clothes his shirt every day at sunrise, and he mentioned for the moon a handful of light from the Throne. So attribution of 'istiwa' to it is for two reasons: one to magnify it by what He mentioned after mentioning His sovereignty in His lordship and creation; and the second to specify it by mention because it is the greatest and most magnificent of creation, according to the known practice of attributing great matters to the greatest things, as it is said: 'The kingship of such-and-such land was completed for so-and-so and he established himself (istawa).'
Source pages p. 669

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of literal interpretations of Allah's being on the Throne (العرش). Maturidi identifies three possible literal meanings: (1) Allah is encompassed by the Throne (إحاطة ذلك به) – which would imply He is limited and lesser than His creation; (2) Allah is equal to the Throne (الاستواء به) – which leads to absurd consequences regarding increase; (3) Allah surpasses the Throne and encompasses it (مجاوزته عنه وإحاطته به) – which suggests need and deficiency in creating something that does not exceed Him, similar to human kings who lack excellence. All three are impossible for Allah. Then he adds that such interpretations lead to division and parts (تجزئة), which are attributes of creatures. Furthermore, physical elevation (ارتفاع المكان) does not confer honor or greatness; a person on a roof is not inherently better than one below if their essence is equal. Therefore, the verse about istiwa cannot refer to literal location. Instead, Maturidi explains that the Throne is a magnificent creation, possibly of light or essence unknown to creation, and the Prophet's hadith about the sun and moon being dressed from the light of the Throne shows its supremacy. The attribution of 'istiwa' to the Throne serves two purposes: (1) to magnify the Throne by mentioning it after Allah's sovereignty, and (2) to specify it as the greatest of creation, similar to saying a king 'established himself' over a kingdom, which means dominion, not physical sitting. Thus, istiwa means al-istila' (dominion) and not literal physical establishment.

Key Terms
الاستواء (istiva/establishment)
إحاطة (encompassment)
تخصيص (specification)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some insist that 'istiwa' must mean literal sitting or physical contact with the Throne.
Correction: Maturidi shows that any such literal interpretation leads to impossibilities like limitation, equality, or deficiency, proving it cannot be literal.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, which of the following is NOT one of the three literal possibilities for 'being on the Throne'?
A) Encompassment by the Throne
B) Equality with the Throne
C) Surpassing and encompassing the Throne
D) Annihilation into the Throne

Key Takeaway
The three literal interpretations of istiwa are all impossible because they imply limitation, need, or creaturely attributes.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite 'ar-Rahmanu 'ala al-arshi istawa', do you catch yourself imagining Allah in a specific location? How does Maturidi's logical refutation expose that assumption as a hidden form of shirk in tawheed? Will you actively train your heart to reject spatial imaginings?
?
You claim Allah is unlike creation, but have you ever secretly thought of Him as 'up there' in the sky? If literal istiwa implies limitation or need, what does that say about your mental picture? Will you commit to purifying your concept of Allah even in casual thoughts?
?
Maturidi argues that literal interpretations reduce Allah to a king who lacks excellence (مَا يَذُمُّ ذَا مِنْ فِعْلِ الْمُلُوكِ). Do you see any resemblance in your own tendency to anthropomorphize God? How can you use this lesson to check your heart whenever you think of Allah in human terms?

Divine Attributes

Further Refutations: Parts and Physical Elevation
Maturidi argues that literalism leads to division and that physical elevation is not a sign of honor.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's additional arguments against literal interpretations of istiwa, specifically regarding division into parts and the nature of physical elevation.

Core Idea
Literal istiwa implies division and attributes of creatures; physical height does not confer honor.

After refuting the three possibilities, Maturidi adds two more arguments: first, that such interpretations lead to dividing Allah into parts (tajzi'a), and second, that physical elevation does not imply true greatness. This lesson explores these arguments that further undermine literalism.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the next portion of the text. Notice the two distinct arguments: one about division (tajzi'a) and one about physical elevation not conferring honor.
The passage flows from the previous refutation.
2
Analyze the division argument
Maturidi says literal interpretation implies 'tajzi'a' (division into parts). Consider why any physical location or spatial relationship forces parts and limits, which are attributes of creatures.
This is a key theological principle: Allah is not composed of parts.
3
Analyze the elevation argument
Maturidi argues that physical height (e.g., on a roof) does not make one inherently honorable or great. Understand his point: honor is not spatial. Therefore, the verse's mention of greatness cannot refer to literal sitting on a high throne.
This refutes the idea that physical elevation implies majesty.
4
Connect to the verse
Note that Maturidi ties this to the Qur'anic context: the verse mentions 'greatness and majesty', so it cannot be about physical location.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, why does physical elevation (like being on a roof) not confer honor?
A) Because the person might fall off
B) Because essence is equal, so elevation is accidental
C) Because the Throne is not physical
D) Because Allah is not like that

Key Takeaway
Literal interpretations of istiwa imply division into parts and falsely equate physical elevation with honor, both of which are impossible for Allah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite or hear the verse 'al-Rahmanu ala al-arsh istawa,' do you ever catch yourself forming a mental image of Allah as seated or located somewhere? How does Maturidi's argument that literal elevation does not confer honor challenge that impulse? What concrete step can you take today to replace that image with a purer understanding of Allah's transcendence?
?
This lesson warns that even well-intentioned attempts to exalt Allah (by imagining Him on a throne) can actually diminish His majesty by reducing Him to creaturely attributes. In what areas of your life might you be tempted to make Allah more familiar or manageable—through routine prayers, comfortable beliefs, or cultural practices? How will you consciously resist that and instead deepen your awe?
?
Maturidi says division (tajzi'a) is a description of creatures. Reflect: Have you ever unconsciously thought of Allah as having parts—like a 'hand' or 'face' in a literal, physical sense? How does knowing that this diminishes His oneness affect your approach to reading anthropomorphic verses? What will you do the next time you encounter such a verse to ensure you uphold tanzih?

The True Meaning: Dominion and the Magnification of the Throne
Maturidi explains the nature of the Throne and the meaning of istiwa as dominion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's positive explanation of istiwa as dominion and the two reasons for attributing it specifically to the Throne.

Core Idea
Istiwa means Allah's complete dominion over the Throne, which is the greatest of creation.

Having refuted literalism, Maturidi provides the correct interpretation. He explains that the Throne is a magnificent creation, possibly of light, and that 'istiwa' is attributed to it for two reasons: to magnify it and to specify it as the greatest creation. The linguistic precedent shows that 'istawa' means to take dominion, as in a king establishing his rule.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the final portion of the text. Notice the mention of the hadith about the sun and moon and the two reasons for attributing istiwa to the Throne.
This is the positive doctrine.
2
Understand the Throne's nature
Maturidi says the verse about creation indicates the Throne's greatness, and it may be of light or essence unknown to creation. Consider why this matters: it avoids corporealism.
3
Analyze the two reasons
The two reasons: (1) to magnify the Throne after mentioning Allah's sovereignty, and (2) to specify it as the greatest creation. This shows the Throne is honored, not that Allah sits on it physically.
This is key to the metaphorical interpretation.
4
Connect to linguistic usage
Maturidi gives the example of saying a king 'istawa' over his kingdom, meaning he has dominion. This clarifies that istiwa means al-istila' (dominion), not physical sitting.
This is the final answer to the question.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Therefore, the verse about istiwa cannot refer to literal location. Instead, Maturidi explains that the Throne is a magnificent creation, possibly of light or essence unknown to creation, and the Prophet's hadith about the sun and moon being dressed from the light of the Throne shows its supremacy. The attribution of 'istiwa' to the Throne serves two purposes: (1) to magnify the Throne by mentioning it after Allah's sovereignty, and (2) to specify it as the greatest of creation, similar to saying a king 'established himself' over a kingdom, which means dominion, not physical sitting. Thus, istiwa means al-istila' (dominion) and not literal physical establishment.

Key Terms
العرش (Throne)
الاستواء (istiva/establishment)
تعظيم (magnification)
تخصيص (specification)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that 'istiwa' in the verse means literal sitting on the Throne as a physical act.
Correction: Maturidi shows it means dominion and completion of power, using the linguistic example of a king 'istawa' over his kingdom.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, what is the correct meaning of 'istiwa' when attributed to Allah?
A) Literal sitting
B) Equality in size
C) Dominion and sovereignty
D) Physical encompassment

Key Takeaway
Istiwa refers to Allah's supreme dominion over the Throne, not a physical location, and the Throne is magnified as the greatest of creation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you say 'Allah is over His Throne,' do you truly feel the weight of His absolute dominion over everything, or do you still unconsciously imagine Him like a king sitting on a chair? How does the truth of istiwa as dominion challenge the way you rely on Allah in your daily worries?
?
If the Throne is the greatest creation, yet it is merely a thing clothed in light by Allah's command, what does that tell you about the insignificance of the earthly problems you magnify in your heart? Will you consciously remind yourself of Allah's unlimited dominion the next time you feel overwhelmed by a situation?
?
You have learned that istiwa means complete control, not a position. Does your prayer reflect that belief? Do you cry out to Allah as if He is near and in control, or do you mechanically recite words without letting His dominion penetrate your soul? What will change in your dua tonight?

Maturidi's Refutation of Istila and Affirmation of Tamam
Maturidi refutes istila and explains istawa as tamam.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Maturidi rejects the interpretation of istawa as conquest and how he instead interprets it as the completion and elevation of divine dominion for the sake of mankind.

Core Idea
Istawa does not mean conquest; it means completion of absolute dominion.

Imam Maturidi confronts a misinterpretation of the Quranic verse 'thumma istawa ala al-arsh' that reduces it to mere conquest or subjugation. He argues that the true meaning involves the completion and elevation of divine kingship, intricately linked to the purpose of creation. This passage lays the foundation for understanding how Maturidi harmonizes divine transcendence with the active role of God in creation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyze it. Then read the English translation to get the general flow of Maturidi's argument.
The opening line is a quotation from an opponent; don't get distracted by unclear references.
2
Identify the two interpretations
Notice that Maturidi first refutes the interpretation of istawa as conquest (istila) by referencing the verse 'Lord of the Mighty Throne'. Then he presents the correct interpretation: completion (tamam) and elevation (uluww) of dominion, supported by multiple Quranic verses.
Pay attention to the shift from 'the other interpretation' to 'as for the interpretation of completion and elevation'.
3
Analyze the Quranic evidence
List the Quranic verses Maturidi uses: the six-day creation cycle, the subjection of creation to humans, and the purpose of worship. See how each verse supports his idea that istawa signifies the perfection of God's kingship for humanity's sake.
Notice the logical connection: creation for mankind, then completion on the seventh day (the day of istawa).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقال آخر: بعد ابن جفنة وابن [؟] ماثل عرشه [؟] والمحاربين تؤملون فلاحاً. قال أبو منصور رحمه الله: ثم الوجه في ذلك لو كان على الاستيلاء، والعرش الملك، إنه مسئول على جميع خلقه، وعلى هذا التأويل المحمول غير هذا، يدل على الأمرين قوله تعالى: ﴿وَهُوَ رَبُّ الْعَرْشِ الْعَظِيمِ﴾ بمعنى الملك العظيم، وفيه إثبات عروش غيره، فذلك يتحتمل ما يحمل ويحف به الملائكة. والله الموفق. وأما على التمام والعلو فهو أن الله تعالى قال: ﴿قُلْ أَئِنَّكُمْ لَتَكْفُرُونَ بِالَّذِي خَلَقَ الْأَرْضَ فِي يَوْمَيْنِ﴾ إلى قوله: ﴿فَقَضَاهُنَّ سَبْعَ سَمَاوَاتٍ﴾ فأخبر بخلق ما ذكر في ستة أيام على التفاريق، ثم أجملها في موضع فقال: ﴿إِنَّ الَّذِي خَلَقَ السَّمَاوَاتِ وَالْأَرْضَ فِي سِتَّةِ أَيَّامٍ ثُمَّ اسْتَوَى عَلَى الْعَرْشِ﴾ بمعنى خلق الممتحن من خلق الأرض والسماوات فيهم ظهر تمام الملك وعلا وارتفع، المقصودون من خلق ما بينا، فبذلك تم معنى الملك وعلا إذا وصل إلى الذين لهم. وقد قبل هذا في خلق البشر خاصة بقوله: ﴿هُوَ الَّذِي خَلَقَ لَكُمْ مَا فِي الْأَرْضِ﴾ وقوله: ﴿وَسَخَّرَ لَكُمُ اللَّيْلَ وَالنَّهَارَ﴾ وقوله: ﴿وَسَخَّرَ لَكُمْ مَا فِي السَّمَاوَاتِ وَمَا فِي الْأَرْضِ﴾. وذكر ابن عباس رضي الله عنه أن البشر خلقوا ليعبدوا الله، واليوم السابع فيه التمام والعلو؛ إذ خلق لهم كل شيء، ويلحق بهم الجن بقوله: ﴿وَمَا خَلَقْتُ الْجِنَّ وَالْإِنْسَ إِلَّا لِيَعْبُدُونِ﴾، لكن المقصود البشر إذ تسخير ما ذكرت كله لهم، ثم بما يرجع إلى منافعهم. والله الموفق.
And another said: ... Then Abu Mansur (may Allah have mercy on him) said: The correct view in that [matter] is that if it were [interpreted] as conquest, and the Throne as kingdom, He is questioned about all His creation, and upon this interpretation that is carried [is] other than this. The two matters are indicated by His statement: 'And He is the Lord of the Mighty Throne' meaning the mighty kingdom, and in it there is proof of other thrones, so that [matter] bears what is carried and surrounded by angels. And Allah is the Grantor of success. As for [the interpretation] of completion and elevation, it is that Allah said: 'Say, do you indeed disbelieve in He who created the earth in two days' until His saying: 'And He completed them as seven heavens' – so He informed of the creation of what was mentioned in six days in detail, then He summarized them in one place and said: 'Indeed, He who created the heavens and the earth in six days then rose over the Throne' meaning He created the trial from the creation of the earth and the heavens – in them appeared the completion of the kingdom and it rose and ascended, the intended ones from the creation as we explained. So by that the meaning of kingdom was completed and rose when it reached those who are for them. And this has been accepted regarding the creation of humans specifically in His saying: 'He is the one who created for you what is on the earth' and His saying: 'And He subjected for you the night and day' and His saying: 'And He subjected for you what is in the heavens and what is on the earth'. And Ibn Abbas (may Allah be pleased with him) mentioned that humans were created to worship Allah, and the seventh day has completion and elevation, since He created everything for them, and the jinn are joined to them by His saying: 'And I did not create the jinn and humans except to worship Me', but the intended are humans since the subjection of all that was mentioned is for them, then [the creation] returns to their benefits. And Allah is the Grantor of success.
Source pages p. 672

Commentary
This passage is a refutation and alternative explanation. Maturidi first responds to an opponent's statement (the unclear poetic line) by stating that if 'istawa' means conquest and 'arsh' means kingdom, then God is questioned about His creation, but the Quranic verse 'Lord of the Mighty Throne' indicates a great kingdom, implying other thrones. Then Maturidi presents the correct interpretation: 'istawa' after creation indicates the completion and elevation of divine dominion, specifically for the sake of mankind. He supports this by citing verses about creation in six days and the subjection of all things to humans. The argument is that the purpose of creation is for humans to worship Allah, and the seventh day (after creation) signifies the completion of dominion for their benefit. The key point is that 'istawa' is not physical elevation but the completion of ultimate kingship.

ملك

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Istawa ala al-arsh means God physically sat or conquered the Throne.
Correction: Maturidi argues that istawa means the completion and elevation of divine dominion, not physical action.

Checkpoint

C) Completion and manifestation of divine dominion for mankind

Key Takeaway
Maturidi interprets istawa as the completion and elevation of God's dominion for the sake of mankind, rejecting any notion of physical conquest or change.

?
The seventh day marks the completion of God's dominion for mankind. Have you ever considered that your existence is not random but a result of God's perfect plan for you to worship Him? How does this change your view of your daily struggles?
