Response to the Objection about Eternal Attributes
Al-Faqih answers the objection that if God is eternally hearing and seeing, then He could also be eternally strangling.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the theological debate about whether divine attributes like 'hearing' and 'seeing' are purely negative or have positive content, and why Al-Faqih prefers explicit negation.

Core Idea
Positive divine attributes can be misleading if they only negate defects.

In this passage, an objector challenges the use of 'eternally hearing' and 'eternally seeing' for God, arguing by analogy that one could then also say 'eternally strangling'. A previous theologian had answered that these terms only negate defects like deafness. Al-Faqih then critiques that answer, arguing that if the attributes only negate, it would be clearer to state the negations directly. This lesson unpacks the objection, the response, and Al-Faqih's critical insight.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection
Read the passage and identify the objection: if God is eternally hearing and seeing, why not also eternally strangling? This is a challenge to the consistency of attributing eternal actions to God.
The objector uses analogy to highlight a potential problem.
2
Understand the initial response
Notice the responder's claim: 'eternally hearing' only negates deafness, and similarly for seeing. He also distinguishes between 'eternally Creator' and saying 'Creator' for a specific act. This is a negative interpretation of the attributes.
The responder tries to avoid attributing any eternal action by making the attributes purely negative.
3
Examine Al-Faqih's critique
Al-Faqih argues that if the attributes only negate defects, then it would be clearer to explicitly say 'not ignorant, not blind, not deaf' instead of using positive terms, because positive terms cause ambiguity.
This critique questions whether the negative interpretation is theologically sufficient.
4
Reflect on the broader implication
Consider why this debate matters: it touches on whether divine attributes have positive content or are merely negations of imperfections. This affects how we understand God's nature.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأجاب لمن عارضه بأنه إذا لم يزل عليها سميعا بصيرا لم لا قلت : إنه لم يزل خانقا ؟ فزعم أن في ذلك إنجاب الخلق في الأزل ، ويعنى بلم يزل سميعا نفي الصمم وما ذلك في العالم والبصير . وزعم أنه يقول : لم يزل الخالق ولا يقول خالقا لما ذكر. قال الفقيه رحمه الله : فإن لم يكن في قوله لم يزل سميعا بصيرا عليها إلا أنه ليس جاهل ولا أعمى ولا أصم فكان التصريح بهذا أولى ؛ إذ هو أبعد من الشبهة
And he answered one who objected to him: If He has eternally been hearing and seeing, why do you not say that He has eternally been strangling? So he claimed that in that is the bringing about of creation in eternity, and he meant by 'eternally hearing' the negation of deafness, and likewise for seeing. And he claimed that he says 'eternally the Creator' but does not say 'Creator' for what was mentioned. Al-Faqih, may God have mercy on him, said: For if his saying 'eternally hearing and seeing' only indicates that He is not ignorant, nor blind, nor deaf, then stating this explicitly would be more appropriate, for it is further from ambiguity.
Source pages p. 727

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer section. An opponent argues: if God is eternally described as 'hearing' and 'seeing,' why not also say He is eternally 'strangling'? The responder (possibly a previous theologian) claimed that 'eternally hearing' means the negation of deafness, not that an action occurs in eternity, and that the term 'eternally Creator' is used differently from saying 'Creator' at a time. Al-Faqih then criticizes this: if the terms 'hearing' and 'seeing' only negate defects, then it would be clearer to state the negations directly (e.g., 'not ignorant, not blind, not deaf') rather than using positive attributes, because positive attributes cause ambiguity. This highlights the theological debate about whether divine attributes are purely negative or have positive content.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that 'eternally hearing' implies a continuous act of hearing in eternity, but the responder claims it only negates deafness.
Correction: The passage shows that the responder interprets the attribute as a negation of defect, not as a positive act, though Al-Faqih criticizes this interpretation.

B) Say 'not deaf' explicitly.
C) Say 'eternally strangling' instead.

Key Takeaway
Positive divine attributes can be misleading if they only negate defects; explicit negation avoids ambiguity.

The Insufficiency of Negative Attributes and Names as Titles
Al-Faqih argues that negative attributes only negate defects and that names without attributes become meaningless titles.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why negative attributes alone are insufficient for describing Allah and why positive attributes must be affirmed.

Core Idea
Negative attributes are not enough; positive attributes are required.

This passage from al-Faqih presents a key argument in Islamic theology: negating defects from Allah does not automatically affirm His positive perfections. The author shows that using names without establishing their corresponding attributes reduces them to empty titles. Let's explore this reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own argument come through before you interpret.
Notice the repetitive phrase 'ولا قوة إلا بالله' appearing twice.
2
Identify the problem with mere negation
Find where al-Faqih says that saying 'not ignorant, not powerless' does not necessarily entail 'powerful, knowing'. Understand why negation alone is insufficient.
3
Understand the orderly acts argument
The passage argues that the orderly system of acts indicates knowledge and power, not just negation of opposites. Reflect on how this refutes relying on negative attributes alone.
This is a key positive evidence for attributes.
4
Grasp the critique of names as titles
Al-Faqih concludes that if attributes are not established, names become mere titles, and saying 'eternally such' becomes meaningless. Consider the implication for how we use divine names.
Titles cannot be eternal because they depend on a relationship.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إذ قد يجوز أن يقال للشيء ليس بجاهل ولا عاجز ولا أصم ، ولا يجب به الوصف بقادر عالم سميع بصير ، فإذا لم يكن في ذا سوى نفي الذي ذكر فحرف النفي أقرب من حرف يفهم ما لا منفعة في فهمه ، بل فيه كل ضرر ، ولو لم يرد بذلك سوى نفي الأضداد فليقل : هو صحيح سليم معافى على نفي الأضداد دون تحقيق الذي ذكر . فإذا لم يجز ذا بان أن الذي زعم من بيان حاصل الذي ذكر أدلة وبعد ، فإن خروج الأفعال المتتابعة على حسن النظام والإحكام هي العلم بها والقدرة عليها لا أنها أدلة من ليس بجاهل ولا عاجز ؛ إذ غير واحد بما وصفه لا يكون منه فعل البته ولا اتساق ، نحو الأعراض كلها ، ولا قوة إلا بالله . على أنها أسماء عن صفات تسقط لسقوط الصفات ، فإذ لم تحقق الصفات صيرت الأسماء أسماء ألقاب ، وإذا صارت كذا فالقول بأنه لم يزل كذا كلام لا معنى له لإحالة اللقب في الأزل ، ولا قوة إلا بالله
Since it may be said of a thing that it is not ignorant, nor powerless, nor deaf, and the description 'powerful, knowing, hearing, seeing' is not necessitated by that. So if there is nothing in this except the negation of what was mentioned, then the particle of negation is closer than a particle that conveys what there is no benefit in understanding, rather it contains every harm. And if he only intended by that the negation of opposites, let him say: He is sound, healthy, well, for the negation of opposites, without the affirmation of what was mentioned. So when this is not permissible, it becomes clear that what he claimed about explaining the result of what was mentioned is evidence. And further, the emergence of successive acts in a good system and order is knowledge of them and power over them, not that they are evidences that He is not ignorant nor powerless; for many a thing described as such does not produce any action at all, nor order, like all accidents. And there is no power except with God. Moreover, they are names that indicate attributes that fall away with the falling away of the attributes; so when the attributes are not established, the names become mere titles. And when they become such, the saying that He is eternally thus is meaningless speech because of the impossibility of a title in eternity. And there is no power except with God.
Source pages p. 728

Commentary
This passage is a detailed argument about the nature of negative and positive attributes. It begins by noting that it is possible to say of something that it is 'not ignorant, not powerless, not deaf' without necessarily implying it is 'powerful, knowing, hearing, seeing.' So if the only content is negation, then it is better to use the negation directly rather than positive terms that might be misunderstood. The author then says that if the purpose is merely to negate opposites, one could say 'sound, healthy, well' instead. But this is not acceptable, which shows that the intended meaning must be more than negation. He then makes a point about orderly acts: the fact that acts come forth in a good system and order indicates knowledge and power, not merely the negation of ignorance and powerlessness. Many things that are not ignorant or powerless (like accidents) do not produce any ordered act. Finally, he argues that names are derived from attributes; if the attributes are not truly established, the names become mere titles (ألقاب), and to say 'eternally such and such' about a title is meaningless because titles cannot be eternal. This reinforces that divine attributes must be real and have positive content.

Key Terms
نفي
صفة
لقب
أزل
أعراض

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Negating defects from Allah is enough to describe Him.
Correction: Negation alone does not establish positive attributes; we must also affirm them, as shown by the orderly acts and the impossibility of eternal titles.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is saying 'He is sound, healthy, well' not sufficient to describe God?
A) Because these terms are not used in the Quran.
B) Because they only negate opposites without affirming positive attributes.
C) Because they imply temporality.
D) Because they are titles, not attributes.

Key Takeaway
Negative attributes are necessary but insufficient; divine names imply real, positive attributes that must be affirmed.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?

?

When you look at the universe around you, do you see it as a proof of what Allah is not, or as a direct testimony of what He is? How can you train your heart to see His positive attributes in everyday signs?
